1.0 Fix Name

webMethods Integration Server 10.15 Core Fix 25.



2.0 Fix ID

IS_10.15_Core_Fix25



3.0 Product(s)/Component(s) Affected

This fix affects webMethods Integration Server 10.15.



4.0 Requirements and Dependencies
IS_10.15_Database_Fix2
IS_10.15_EmbeddedDB_Fix2
TPP_10.15_SpringFramework_Fix1
TPP_10.15_Parsers_Fix6
TPP_10.15_Swagger_Fix3
CJP_10.15_Fix354
ZSL_10.15_Fix2
TPP_10.15_BaseSecurity_Fix2
WAR_10.15_Fix4



5.0 Platform Support

webMethods Integration Server 10.15 Core Fix 25 is supported on the 
same platforms and operating systems and with the same JREs as webMethods 
Integration Server 10.15.



6.0 Cautions and Warnings

If Integration Server uses central user management which is provided through My 
webMethods Server, you must keep the common libraries provided by My webMethods 
Server up to date. To obtain the current changes to the common libraries, install 
the latest My webMethods Server fix located under Common Libraries in IBM 
webMethods Update Manager.

IS_10.15_Core_Fix18 (or higher) and IS_10.15_WmAdmin_Fix4 (or higher) are 
interdependent. Therefore, install both the fixes together.

IS_10.15_Core_Fix18 (or higher) and IS_10.15_WmCloud_Fix5 (or higher) are 
interdependent. Therefore, install both the fixes together.

After installing fix IS_10.15_Core_Fix12 (or higher) and its required dependent 
fixes (CJP_10.15_Fix354 or higher), Integration Server 10.15 uses Azul Java 
version 17.50 for runtime. All future fixes for Integration Server will require 
and work on Java 17 runtime only. Products running on AIX use IBM Semeru Java 
17.0.9.

IS_10.15_Core_Fix20 (or higher) depends on TPP_10.15_BaseSecurity_Fix2 and 
ZSL_10.15_Fix2. Integration Server does not start if these two fixes are not 
installed. In addition, IBM Update Manager installs all three fixes automatically.

IS_10.15_Core_Fix21 (or higher) and Web Services Stack Core 10.15.0 Fix 11 (or 
higher) fixes are interdependent. Apply them together to fully resolve PIE-97963.



7.0 Fix Contents

PIE-100280
Integration Server now includes container script options and an environment
variable to control where the Integration Server running in a container writes
audit logs to the files system and the console. 

When creating an Integration Server image using the is_container script, use the
-Dlog <destination> argument to specify where Integration Server writes the
server log information for this session. Specify one of the following for
<destination>: 

- <filename>: Specify the fully qualified path or relative path to the file in
which you want the server to write server log information for this session.
Relative path is relative to the Integration Server home directory: Integration
Server_directory \instances\<instance_name> 
The filename must specify a directory and filename.  The default destination is
controlled by the watt.debug.logfile server configuration parameter 

- none: Write server log information to the computer screen (STDOUT).Server log
messages written to STDOUT include the identifier “ISSERVER” to help
differentiate server log messages from other messages written to the console. 

- both: Write server log information to the computer screen (STDOUT) and to the
destination specified by the watt.debug.logfile parameter. This is the default
value 

Use -Dlogformat <format> argument to specify JSON as the format to which
Integration Server converts the server log and audit log entries written to the
console (STDOUT or computer screen). Specify <format> as json. Integration
Server supports only "json" format. 

When starting a container for an Integration Server image, use the
WM_IS_LOG_DESTINATION environment variable to override the log destination
specified in the image. The WM_IS_LOG_DESTINATION environment variable has the
same possible values as the -Dlog <destination> argument described above. 

To specify that a container use the JSON format for server log entries and audit
log entries, when starting a container for Integration Server image, set the
LOG_FORMAT environment variable to json. 

PIE-100687
REST requests or responses fail when date fields include a time component
(yyyy-MM-ddThh:mm:ss) instead of using the expected date-only format
(yyyy-MM-dd). 

Integration Server strictly enforces the yyyy-MM-dd format for properties
defined as string with format: date. When clients send date-time values
(2025-11-03T00:00:00), Integration Server, acting as a provider, fails to parse
them, resulting in REST validation errors and payload rejection. As a consumer,
Integration Server encounters invalid datatype errors when it receives such
values in responses. 

This issue is now resolved by adding the watt.server.rest.dateFormat.strict
server parameter. 

watt.server.rest.dateFormat.strict

Specifies how strictly Integration Server validates date strings in REST APIs.
When set to true, Integration Server enforces the yyyy-MM-dd format for
properties defined as string with format: date. When set to false, the server
accepts both yyyy-MM-dd and yyyy-MM-dd'T'HH:mm:ss formats, allowing limited
flexibility. The default value is true. 
You do not need to restart Integration Server for this parameter change to take
effect. 

PIE-101109
The bc-fips, bcmail-fips, bcpg-fips, and bcpkix-fips JARs in Integration Server
are upgraded to address the security vulnerability CVE-2025-8916.

PIE-101442
Integration Server throws Access Denied exception during SOAP requests because
sessions created for these calls are not stored in the 
cluster (Terracotta Server Array) and are removed after processing.

The session handling logic causes this issue because it skips saving the SOAP
sessions in the cluster (Terracotta Server Array).

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-101863
The jcode utility in Integration Server throws a compilation error while
compiling a Java service.

The classpath in the jcode utility does not include all the JAR files
necessary to compile services that depend on external libraries.
As a result, service compilation fails.

This issue is resolved. Now, the jcode utility includes the JARs
from the Integration Server classpath.

PIE-101910
In a cluster, a request to validate an OAuth access token returns an OAuth token
that has been deleted. 

In a cluster, an OAuth token deleted on one server might still be in the local
cache of another server. A request to validate an access token might result in
Integration Server returning a deleted token. 

To resolve this issue, when an Integration Server in a cluster receives a
request to validate an access token, the Integration Server first checks if the
access token is available in the shared database. If the token is not there,
Integration Server checks to see if the token in in the local cache. If it is,
Integration Server removes the token from the local caches. This prevents
Integration Server from returning a deleted token from the local cache. 

PIE-101913
When the cached service output has no signature output fields, the cache
includes the whole pipeline even when strict mode is enabled for service
caching. 

The behavior of service caching with strict caching enabled is now modified to
return an empty pipeline when the cached service output does not contain
signature output fields. To enable the modified behavior, use the new
watt.server.serviceResults.cache.strict.returnOutputSigOrEmpty parameter. 

When strict caching is enabled and the
watt.server.serviceResults.cache.strict.returnOutputSigOrEmpty parameter is set
to "true", the flow service returns an empty pipeline. The default value is
false. If this parameter is set to false, the output returns the default
pipeline when the pipeline does not contain signature output fields. If you have
run the flow service without the new parameter, you must reset the cache to
enable the new behavior. For details about resetting the cache, see the topic
about caching service results in the Integration Server documentation. You can
also restart Integration Server to clear the cache. 

PIE-101914
The pub.security:decrypt and pub.security:decryptAndVerify services fail with
the error: The service could not retrieve the secret key.

This issue occurs when the encrypted data contains multiple public key encrypted
data packets, and the pgpSecretKey is not found in the first packet.

The issue is now resolved. 

PIE-102010
The assets page in the Integration Server Administrator console
allows access without authentication.

The Administrator console exposes an assets endpoint at
<http://<hostname>:<port>/assets, which a user can access only
when watt.server.displayDirectories is true and the user is logged in.
When the user opens this page without logging in, the page prompts for
credentials. However, if the user clicks Cancel, authentication is
bypassed and the assets directory becomes visible. This behavior
occurs whether the browser stores the login or not.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-102432
The pub.client.ldap:delete service returns HTTP 200 OK status code even when
the LDAP server does not find the specified DN.

This issue occurs because the service does not raise an error when the requested
DN is missing in the LDAP directory. The HTTP status reflects only the
successful 
execution of the service, not the LDAP operation outcome.

This issue is now resolved. The service introduces a new input parameter
"failIfNotFound". When you set this parameter to yes, the service returns an
error if the DN does not exist in the LDAP directory. If you do not specify the
parameter or set it to no, the service continues with the existing behavior.

PIE-102450
This fix includes webMethods Application Manager, which is a new CLI tool that
can generate 
Dockerfiles from an existing webMethods Integration project or edge runtime. For
 more information, 
see the "weMethods Application Manager CLI Reference guide" in the Integration
Server documentation. 

This fix also introduces the following enhancements to the webMethods Package
Manager CLI tool: 
- The "-v|--version" option displays the version of the wpm CLI tool in the
format 
major.minor.patch.buildNumber, along with the Integration Server build number. 
- The "wpm list" command displays a list of packages available in the IBM
webMethods Package Registry. 
For more information about how you can filter the displayed results, see the
"webMethods Package 
Manager CLI Reference" guide in the Integration Server documentation.
- The ability to include a custom HTTPS port when providing the URL for а -r,
-ws, or -wr argument. 

PIE-102517
Integration Server logs the registration-port password in plain text, 
creating a security risk.

When the Enterprise Gateway facility logger (0079) runs at TRACE level, 
the server log displays the registration-port password in clear text.

This issue is resolved. Now, the password is masked in the server log. 

PIE-102549
Integration Server exposes submitted passwords in clear text after an account
locks due to multiple failed login attempts.

When account locking is enabled, Integration Server returns passwords provided
by users in later responses, after the account locks. This behavior discloses
credentials and puts users at risk especially if they reuse the passwords.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-102753
The pub.client:smtp service sends emails with unreadable attachment filenames.

The issue occurs because the service encodes filenames before sending messages.
So, filenames that are long or have special characters look corrupt to
recipients. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-102778
Scheduled tasks intermittently remain stuck in Running state after
executing their service, preventing subsequent runs from triggering.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-103138
The com.wm.data.DataElement class has been added to the Integration Server
whitelist configuration file whitelistclasses.xml. 

PIE-103217
Integration Server uses version 1.0.2.5 of the third-party FIPS-compliant Bouncy
Castle cryptographic 
library that contains a known security vulnerability.

The issue is resolved. Integration Server now uses version 2.1.2 of the Bouncy
Castle library. 

PIE-103261
Certified container images for Integration Server (IS) and Microservices Runtime
(MSR) now use the ubi9-minimal STIG-ready image. 

With this fix, the ubi9-minimal STIG-ready image, certified by FedRAMP as a base
image, replaces the Red Hat Universal Base Image 9 Minimal (ubi9-minimal) base
image that the certified container images for IS and MSR used previously. The
ubi9-minimal STIG-ready image is an internal hardened image, created by the
FedRAMP team and published to the IBM Cloud Container Registry (ICR). The
ubi9-minimal STIG-ready image is now the base image for the IS and MSR images
that are published to the ICR registry. 

For details about the docker build commands used for IS images, see the topic
about building the docker image for an Integration Server instance in the
Integration Server documentation. 

PIE-103401
REST service invocations fail with a NullPointerException when the Accept header
specifies an 
unrecognized content type with a character set.

The issue is resolved.

PIE-96632
The Swagger 2.0 document generated for a REST API Descriptor has HTTP response
codes in the wrong order for some GET endpoints. 

The document does not maintain the ascending order of HTTP response codes
for some GET endpoints. For example, "404 Not Found"
appears after "500 Internal Server Error", which creates confusion when
reviewing API behavior and response flows.

This issue is now resolved. 

Note: This fix applies only to new services generated from the Swagger file.

PIE-97728
Changes to metering to count top-level invocations of the services
wm.prt.status:handleChangeCommand and wm.prt.dispatch:handleTransition as
transactions. 

PIE-98285
Integration Server logs the error message "Unable to find message key '162.9001'
in bundle 'com.wm.app.b2b.server.util.data.ehcache.resources.
EhcacheDataMessageBundle'" instead of the intended message 
"Critical Error: Cache <cacheName> element evicted for 
key=<key1> value type=<valuetype> {3}."

This issue occurs when the cache is evicted at server startup. Integration
Server attempts to log the cache eviction event but does not find the corresponding
message text in the EhcacheDataMessageBundle resource file. As a result, the 
server log displays the "Unable to find message key…" error instead of the 
meaningful cache eviction message.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-98650
Designer freezes during variable search (Ctrl+F) in complex pipeline documents.

Designer freezes when searching for variables in deeply nested documents with a
large number of doctypes, especially if the variable is missing or located near
the end. The search logic fails to handle large and deeply nested structures,
causing infinite traversal and UI failure. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-99000
Creating an email port through application.properties using dynamic variables
fails because Integration Server does not correctly handle the listener password
and omits the package property in listeners.cnf, leading to authentication
errors. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-100200 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix24)
Integration Server throws the error "Cannot assign field 'gLoop' because 
'this.gState' is null" when you update the Enterprise Gateway external port.

Integration Server displays this error message when Enterprise Gateway Server
experiences high load.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-100300 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix24)
Integration Server no longer automatically uses distributed caches for system
caches when the Integration Server belongs to a cluster. 

Previously, if an Integration Server was configured to be in a cluster,
Integration Server automatically made each system cache a distributed cache even
if Integration Server used local caches only. 

Now, when an Integration Server belongs to a cluster, Integration Server sets
system cache managers to use distributed caches if at least one system cache is
a distributed cache. If all the system caches are local caches, Integration
Server does not configure the system cache manager to use distributed caches. 

PIE-100672 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix24)
After applying fixes that include PIE-88454 and PIE-88393, JDBC connection 
metadata for expired connections leaks from the JDBC connection pool.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-100784 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix24)
JDBC connection leak under heavy load or after a SQLException occurs.

Under heavy load, Integration Server might leak JDBC connections from a JDBC
connection pool. A connection leak can also occur when the JDBC connection
raises a SQLException while clearing warnings. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-101013 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix24)
Integration Server does not write audit logs to the console despite being
configured to do so. 

When the environment variable SAG_IS_AUDIT_STDOUT_LOGGER specifies the audit
logs to write to the console and watt.server.audit.logFilesToKeep=1, Integration
Server does not write audit logs to the console. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-101107 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix24)
REST requests using the RAD directive fail if the Authorization header lacks
an authorization type.

Integration Server requires an authorization type in the Authorization header
and returns a 401 Unauthorized response when it is missing.

This issue is resolved. Integration Server now defaults to Basic authentication
when the Authorization header does not specify a type, preventing 401
Unauthorized responses.

PIE-101164 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix24)
After applying a fix that includes PIE-87159, the Swagger 2.0 documents that
Integration Server generates contain additional lines that impact consuming
applications. 

The following line is added for every object in the Swagger 2.0 document
generated from a REST API Descriptor: 

type: object

The additional object can change the way the REST API Descriptor is consumed by
other applications. According to the Swagger specification, the absence of the
type results in undefined behavior 

To resolve this issue, Integration Server now includes a server configuration
parameter to control whether the type:object is added for objects in Swagger 2.0
documents. 

watt.server.rest.swagger.setTypeForAllObjects
Specifies whether a Swagger 2.0 document generated for a REST API Descriptor
explicitly sets the type to object for objects. Set this parameter to false to
generate Swagger 2.0 documents in the same manner as older releases which do not
include PIE-87159. Leave this parameter blank to maintain the current behavior
which includes explicitly specifying the type of all objects. 

Changes to this parameter take effect the next time integration Server generates
a Swagger 2.0 document for the REST API Descriptors. 

The watt.server.rest.swagger.setTypeForAllObjects parameter does not impact
OpenAPI 3 documents (Swagger 3.0) generated for REST API Descriptors. 

PIE-101165 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix24)
Creating signed and encrypted S/MIME data using the 
pub.smime.keystore:createSignedAndEncryptedData service results in invalid
output. 

When using the pub.smime.keystore:createSignedAndEncryptedData service to create
signed and encrypted S/MIME messages, Integration Server generates an invalid
signed S/MIME message containing duplicate MIME headers with conflicting values.
The issue is because of the changes in header handling behavior introduced
during the transition to Bouncy Castle JARs.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-101357 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix24)
After applying a fix that includes PIE-88419, an Enterprise Gateway
configuration sometimes resolves OPTIONS preflight requests on the Internal
Server instead of the Enterprise Gateway Server. 
 
The resolution to PIE-88419 causes an Enterprise Gateway Server to forward an
OPTIONS request to the Internal Integration Server when CORS is enabled. The
Internal Integration Server then resolves the request. Prior to installing
PIE-88419, the Enterprise Gateway Server resolved an OIPTIONS request. 
 
The behavior introduced with PIE-88419 is now removed.

PIE-101493 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix24)
Changes to how Integration Server handles errors that occur while backing up the
config directory during the server initialization process. 

During server initialization, Integration Server attempts to back up the
<IntegrationServer>/instances/<instanceName>/config directory. If an attempt to
back up a file or directory within the config directory fails, Integration
Server does not back up any more items and continues with server initialization.
However, insufficient file permissions or unexpected errors that occur while
backing up the config directory might cause Integration Server to become
unresponsive and prevent server initialization. 

To improve the server initialization process, if an error occurs while backing
up a specific file or directory, Integration Server now logs the exception and
the process of backing up the config directory continues. 

PIE-101672 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix24)
Integration Server now provides wm.broker.util:changeBrokerTriggerState to 
enable or disable broker triggers.

PIE-101907 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix24)
Integration Server appears to be unresponsive, but ports are active and
listening for requests. 

Threads generating UUIDs stalled, creating thread contention which prevented
Integration Server from processing new requests. Integration Server appeared to
become unresponsive despite having active ports. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-102285
You can now print out the Integration Server logs only to the console to free
storage space on the file system. 

When you start Integration Server from the command prompt, use the "-log none
-logformat json" switch to print out the log entries from the following logs
only to the console in the JSON format: 

audit log files, such as WMERROR, WMSERVICE
server.log

If you use just the "-log none" switch, the server log entries are printed out
to the console, but the audit log entries are sent to the console and saved as
log files on the file system. 

To reduce the length of messages printed to the console, you can use the
watt.server.log.shortKey parameter to shorten the key names in the
JSON-formatted log messages.

PIE-102358
Updates to Integration Server to provide a list of values for server
configuration parameters and environment variables to webMethods Integration
(SaaS). 

PIE-102594
Integration Server now supports JWT signature verification using public keys
retrieved from a JSON Web Key Set (JWKS) endpoint.

Configure a JWKS endpoint for each trusted issuer, and Integration Server
automatically downloads and refreshes the issuer’s public keys for signature
verification.

This enhancement eliminates the need to manually update the truststore when
issuers rotate their keys. 
For more information, see the webMethods Integration Server Administrator's
Guide. 

PIE-102695
When using the getConnection() method to get a connection from a JDBC connection 
pool, the method returns the connection that is currently in use and is not 
released back to the pool yet.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-98736 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix24)
Integration Server throws a compilation error while compiling Java services in
a package when the Java compiler version differs from the Java version of the
JVM running Integration Server.

If the watt.server.compile parameter points to an external Java compiler that
uses a different Java version than the JVM running Integration Server, the
mismatch causes the compilation to fail.

This issue is now resolved. The watt.server.compile parameter now uses the
Java compiler from the JDK bundled with Integration Server as the default value.

PIE-99207 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix24)
Integration Server provides a new public service, 
pub.utils.messaging:listOutOfSyncProtobufDocs. This service compares protocol 
buffers between Integration Server and Universal Messaging for publishable documents.
The service accepts the following input parameters:

packageNames (String List, Optional): List of package names. The service scans 
documents within these packages to compare IS and UM protobuf descriptors.

documentTypeNames (String List, Optional): List of document type names. The 
service limits the comparison to these specified document type names.

decompile (String, Optional): Specifies whether the service generates reverse 
.proto files from compiled binaries. If true, generates reverse .proto files 
from compiled binaries. The default value is false.

protoFileLocation (String, Conditional): Specifies the location to store .proto 
files. Required only if decompile is true. If the path does not exist, 
Integration Server attempts to create the folder structure. If the server fails 
to create the folder, it throws an error.

All input parameters are optional. If you do not provide any input values, the
service compares all publishable documents on the server and generates a report, 
which can be resource-intensive based on the number of documents and packages.

Output Parameter:

outOfSync (Document List): A list of documents where IS and UM protobuf 
descriptors are not in sync. Each entry includes:

package (String): Name of the package containing the document.

documentName (String): Name of the document type.

channelName (String): Associated channel name.

protoFileName (String): Name of the .proto file (if applicable).

error (String): Description of the mismatch or error encountered.

The output signature remains same whether you provide the input parameters or 
not. The service displays these results as part of its output.

Usage Notes:

- If decompile is true and protoFileLocation is missing, the service returns an 
  error.

- Protocol buffers are supported only for Universal Messaging. This service 
  works only for documents synced with UM.

PIE-99556 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix24)
Integration Server throws the “Unable to locate or start compiler” error
when you save a Java service in Designer.

To compile a Java service, Integration Server runs the javac command based on
the value of the "watt.server.compile" parameter, which defaults to
"javac -classpath {0} -d {1} {2}". When the server’s classpath includes multiple
JAR files, the length of the resulting command exceeds the Windows command line
limit of 32,000 characters. Therefore, Integration Server fails to run the
command. 

This issue is resolved. Now, Integration Server passes compiler arguments
through a temporary file instead of directly on the command line. To compile a 
Java service, Integration Server creates a temporary file with the required 
arguments, runs the command using the "javac @<tempfile>" syntax, and deletes 
the file after execution (regardless of whether the command is successful or not). |
This method avoids the Windows character limit and ensures that Java services 
compile successfully.

PIE-100450 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
The Searchable checkbox does not appear on the Edit cache page for the TnDocType
system cache. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-100512 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
The watt.server.oauth.authCode.expirySeconds parameter cannot be set to -1.

When watt.server.oauth.authCode.expirySeconds is set to -1, authorization codes
never expire. However, validation logic prevented setting the value to -1. 

This issue is now resolved. The validation logic for
watt.server.oauth.authCode.expirySeconds now allows the value to be -1 or a
positive integer greater than or equal to 60. 

When watt.server.oauth.authCode.expirySeconds is set to -1, the Remove Expired
Tokens system task is removed. 

PIE-100552 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
The diagnostic archive generated by the diagnostic utility now includes the JPS
module configuration settings for the JVM. 

The config/JavaModules.txt file in the diagnostic archive contains JPS module
configuration. This information can help diagnose runtime Java permission errors
caused by failed attempts to invoke Java code protected by this module. 

PIE-100577 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
Integration Server fails to log the packages it loads during startup, which
makes debugging difficult.

Integration Server does not log the packages it loads at startup, which makes it
hard to trace loaded packages and debug when packages exist on the disk but
fail to load.

This issue is now resolved. The server logs packages loaded at startup,
improving traceability and debugging.

PIE-100583 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
ACL checking does not work for members of an LDAP group that was created using a
configuration variables template (application.properties file). 

If an LDAP group was created by applying a configuration variables template, ACL
checking for members of the group is successful only when the groupName portion
of the ldapgroup.<groupName>.dn key is the same as the group name in the
distinguished name. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-100657 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
The pub.flow:restorePipelineFromFile service sometimes fails with a
NoSuchMethodException when the service restores an XML pipeline 

This issue is now resolved. 

PIE-100670 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
The pub.client:soapClient service does not consistently enforce the timeout set
on the INVOKE step. 

This issue is now resolved. Integration Server enforces the timeout setting for
the INVOKE step. 

This resolution also corrects an issue where a SOAP call from API Gateway did
not have a timeout value. 

PIE-100684 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
Integration Server Administrator does not show the alert message “Restart is
required for changes to take effect” immediately after saving extended settings.
The message appears only after the user manually refreshes the browser, which
confuses administrators. 

Integration Server Administrator does not refresh the masthead when extended
settings are updated. As a result, the restart notification remains hidden until
the page reloads. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-100798 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
After switching from Entrust to Bouncy Castle libraries, processing SMIME
messages with pub.smime.keystore:processEncryptedData throws “Could not retrieve 
content from input” for some inputs.

The decryption failures result from differences in how Bouncy Castle library
parses encrypted SMIME data.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-100897 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
Support for a 16 byte salt for password encryption.

Integration Server can now use a 16 byte salt for password encryption. Set the
new server configuration parameter watt.server.auth.password.saltLength to 16 to
use a 16 byte salt. Set the parameter to 8 to use an 8 byte salt. The default
value is 8. 

Integration Server must be restarted for changes to take effect.

After the watt.server.auth.password.saltLength parameter value is changed,
Integration Server uses the new value for encrypting new passwords. Existing
passwords that use the previous salt length continue to work. 

PIE-100988 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
PGP encryption fails when the pub.security:encrypt service selects an expired
key from the keyring as the first key for encryption. The service throws an
exception even though the keyring contains another valid key.

The failure occurs because the updated Bouncy Castle libraries in
Integration Server change the key selection behavior.

This issue is resolved. The service now uses the first valid non-expired public
key for encryption.

PIE-101101 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
The WmPublic and WmRoot packages contain an extraneous folder named recordimpl.

The recordimpl folder no longer appears in the WmPublic and WmRoot packages.

PIE-101109
The bc-fips, bcmail-fips, bcpg-fips, and bcpkix-fips JARs in Integration Server
are upgraded to address the security vulnerability CVE-2025-8916.

PIE-101139 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
The fix for PIE-98290 did not use the correct name for the server configuration
parameters. 

While the readme text for PIE-98290 included the correct server configuration
parameter names, the fix did not use the correct names. 

The server configuration parameter names have been changed. 

watt.server.statisticsDataCollector.deletionInterval is now
watt.server.statisticsDataCollector.removal.interval 
watt.server.statisticsDataCollector.deletionInterval.batchSize is now
watt.server.statisticsDataCollector.removal.rows 

PIE-101171 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
Integration Server does not log failures during the migration of the password
store. 

The migration utility logs a general failure message but does not indicate
specific issues related to the password store migration.

This issue is now resolved. Integration Server records password store migration
errors in the migrationLog.txt file.

PIE-101664 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
An Integration Server that is configured as an Internal Server sporadically
throws a StringIndexOutOfBoundsException. 

When an Integration Server is configured as an Internal Server for an Enterprise
Gateway, the Internal Server might throw a StringIndexOutOfBoundsException when
reading the response to an authentication request and the response does not
contain any data. 

Now, an Internal Server no longer throws a StringIndexOutOfBoundsException when
the response does not contain any data. 

PIE-80907 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
The pub.client.ldap:search service enters an infinite loop when run with 
pageSize. 

Integration Server uses the ldapCookie returned by the LDAP server while 
performing paged searches using pub.client.ldap:search. The LDAP 
server must return null when there are no entries to return to Integration
Server. However, pub.client.ldap:search does not receive null and enters an
infinite loop when run with pageSize. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-95728 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
Integration Server throws detailed error messages whenever it fails to enable or
disable JMS connections, disclosing security-related information such as
environment details and configuration data.

This issue is now resolved. Integration Server now displays generic error
messages. 

PIE-97062 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
In a stateless cluster, an OAuth client or scope that was created, updated, or
deleted on one server might not be reflected on another server in the cluster. 

Integration Server fetches client and scope information from a local cache. In a
stateless cluster, OAuth client and scope information is stored in a database.
At startup, each Integration Server in a stateless cluster synchronizes the
local caches with the database to obtain the latest updates.  If an Integration
Server has not recently reloaded the local caches, changes made to OAuth clients
and scopes by other Integration Servers in the cluster are not available in the
local cache. 

Integration Server now reloads the local client cache and scope cache after
creating, updating, or deleting a client or scope. This reduces the window for
which the local cache information is out of sync with the database. 

PIE-97787 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
The pub.client.ftp:get service throws java.net.SocketException:
Socket is Closed.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-98170 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
Integration Server restricts the value of
watt.server.http.Content-Security-Policy to script-src 'self' 'unsafe-inline',
which limits administrators from using other valid Content-Security-Policy
values.

This issue is now resolved by updating the behavior of the parameter. The
parameter now accepts any valid Content-Security-Policy value.

Note: The Integration Server Administrator includes pages that are built by
using different technologies. Some pages display correctly only with
script-src 'self' 'unsafe-inline'. If you use a different value and the pages
do not work as expected, you can reset the parameter.
For more information about watt.server.http.Content-Security-Policy, see IBM
webMethods Integration Server Administrator's Guide.

PIE-98464 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
The pub.json:documentToJSONString service fails when the encodeDateAs input
parameter uses a custom date format.

Redundant validation of the encodeDateAs parameter causes the issue.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-99150 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
Integration Server sanitizes and returns user-supplied data in the response
when the Integration Server Administrator invokes the login service with invalid
input, which can lead to content injection or phishing risks.

This issue is now resolved. The service no longer returns any part of the input
and logs the sanitized data in the server and security logs.

PIE-99189 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
Changes to the pub.utils:deepClone service to prevent the deserialization of
unsafe Java objects. 

The pub.utils:deepClone service performs a deep clone of an object using the
default Java serialization mechanism. For standard Java objects, such as a
String, Double, and [] (array), the service now performs a deep clone if the
Java object is serializable. For custom Java objects, the service can now use a
whitelist filter to prevent the deserialization of unsafe Java objects. The
service only clones the object if the class appears in the whitelist. 

The pub.utils:deepClone service performs whitelist filtering when the
watt.server.checkWhitelist parameter is set to true. 

PIE-99473 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
Integration Server now caches cryptographic hashed passwords which might improve
performance. 

When Integration Server must repeatedly authenticate the same user, the multiple
calls for authentication can impact performance. By storing cryptographic hashed
passwords in a local cache, Integration Server might demonstrate a performance
improvement. 

PIE-99490 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
Integration Server does not release JDBC connections, increasing the risk of 
potential resource leaks.

After applying a fix that includes PIE-88393, causes Integration Server not to 
release JDBC connections.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-99601 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
Integration Server returns header parameter values and omits body parameters
for a REST API POST request.

In REST API POST requests, Integration Server gives precedence to header
parameters over body parameters when both contain the same names. Therefore,
Integration Server includes only the header values in the response and
ignores the corresponding body parameters.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-99848 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix23)
The pub.string:messageFormat service does not handle single quotes correctly.

This fix resolves two issues surrounding the use of single quotes in the pattern 
string for pub.string:messageFormat.

- When a literal single quote appears in a pattern string, the 
pub.string:messageFormat service removed the single quote which resulted in 
missing characters in the output. Now, during service execution, the 
pub.string:messageFormat service replaces a single quote between two letters in 
a pattern string with two single quotes as part of processing. This ensures that 
the output contains the single quote.

Note: The pub.string:messageFormat service does not replace two single quotes 
between two letters with four single quotes.

- When single quotes are used with a placeholder in a pattern, the 
pub.string:messageFormat service does not replace the placeholder. The 
pub.string:messageFormat now handles single quotes with placeholders correctly.

Note: To ensure the correct output when using single quotes in placeholder 
patterns, format the patterns according to the Java.Text.MessageFormat syntax.

Run-time errors caused by health indicators resulted in a large number of active
threads that will never shut down and eventually cause out of memory errors.

watt.server.serverlogFilesToKeep server configuration parameter. However, this

instead of a real directory.

Transport-Security)

-Policy)
X-Permitted-Cross-Domain-Policies (configured by using watt.server.http.X-
Permitted-Cross-Domain-Policies)

PIE-98917 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix22)
Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF) vulnerability found in
pub.client.oauth:executeRequest service. 
 
The resourceUri input parameter for the pub.client.oauth:executeRequest service
points to the resource that the client application wants to access on the
resource server. The service accepts any URI which results in Integration Server
attempting to access the URI. This is an SSRF vulnerability 
 
To resolve this vulnerability, Integration Server now uses an allow list with
the pub.client.oauth:executeRequest service. If the URI does not appear in the
allow list, the service ends with a ServiceException. 
 
Integration Server introduces two server configuration parameters for enabling
and specifying the allow list for pub.client.oauth:executeRequest. 
 
watt.client.oauth.allowlist.enabled
Specifies whether Integration Server uses an allow list with the
pub.client.oauth:executeRequest service. Set this parameter to true to use the
allow list defined by the watt.client.oauth.allowlist.allowedServers parameter.
Set this parameter false if you do not want to use an allow list. A value of
false leaves the pub.client.oauth:executeRequest service vulnerable to a
Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF).  The default value is true. 
 
Integration Server does not need to be restarted for changes to this parameter
to take effect. 
 
watt.client.oauth.allowlist.allowedServers
Specifies the URIs that can be accessed by the pub.client.oauth:executeRequest
service. When an allow list is used with the service, the value of the
resourceUri input parameter must appear in the list for Integration Server to
attempt to access the URI. If the URI is not in the allow list, the service ends
with a ServiceException that states “<resourceName> resource cannot be accessed.
The resource is not on the allow list.” 

The watt.client.oauth.allowlist.enabled must be set to true for the allow list
to be enforced. 
 
Integration Server does not need to be restarted for changes to this parameter
to take effect. 

You can set this parameter to a comma- or space-separated list of URIs or the
absolute path to a file. You cannot specify a combination of these. 

To define this parameter using a comma- or space- separated list of URIs, enter
protocol://hostname or protocol://hostname:portnumber. You can specify the IP
address or the name of the machine for hostname. The values are case-sensitive.
Use a space or comma delimiter to specify multiple values. 

To define this parameter using a text file set the value to:
file:pathToFile\filename

For example:
watt.client.oauth.allowlist.allowedServers=file:c:\oauth\allowedUriList.txt 

The file must use the same syntax as is required for the
watt.client.oauth.allowlist.allowedServers with the difference that each line
must be an allowed URI or a regular expression. 

Note: The IP address and host name cannot be used interchangeably. For example,
if you specify a host name, and the resourceUri uses the corresponding IP
address, the pub.client.oauth:executeRequest service ends with an error. 

You can use an asterisk (*) to indicate that any URI is allowed.

You can also use regular expressions in the comma-separated list of allowed URIs
which can make the list of URIs easier to maintain. Integration Server treats
any value in the comma-separated list that begins with "r:" as a regular
expression. Integration Server treats any value that does not begin with "r:" as
a simple string. The server configuration parameter uses the Java regular
expression syntax, as documented at Pattern (Java Platform SE 7 ) . 

A regular expression value must match the entire value of the supplied
resourceUri value for it to be considered a match. 

Example:

watt.client.oauth.allowlist.allowedServers=http://test1.domain.com,r:https?://.*.test2.domain.com:[0-9]+,r:.+\.[a-zA-Z]*-int.domain.com

Integration Server treats the first value, http://test1.domain.com, as a simple
string. If a resourceUri is set to this value, the
pub.client.oauth:executeRequest service attempts to access the URI. 

The second value, "r:https?://.*.test2.domain.com:[0-9]+", contains a regular
expression. The "r:" is not part of the regular expression. The actual regular
expression used to match the supplied resourceUri is
"https?://.*.test2.domain.com:[0-9]+". 

The third value, "r:.+\.[a-zA-Z]*-int.domain.com", contains a regular
expression. The "r:" is not part of the regular expression. The actual regular
expression used to match the supplied resourceUri is
".+\.[a-zA-Z]*-int.domain.com". 

resourceUri: http://test1.domain.com will be accessed because it is equal to the
first value. 
resourceUri: http://my.test2.domain.com:8080 will be accessed because it matches
the second value. 
resourceUri: https://my.test2.domain.com:8088 will be accessed because it
matches the second value. 
resourceURI: http://my.test2.domain.com will not be accessed. If it had a port
number, it would match the second value. 
resourceUri: nbps://example.prod-int.domain.com will be accessed because it
matches the third value. 
resourceUri: example.qa.staging-int.domain.com" will be accessed because it
matches the third value. 
resourceUri: example.dev1-int.domain.com" will not be accessed. If the second
token of the host name did not include any digits, it would have matched the
third value. 

Regular expressions that match any host name, IP address and port (e.g. "r:.+"
and "r:.*") will have the same effect as "*". 

Note: When an allow list is enabled for pub.client.oauth:executeRequest,
Integration Server evaluates the list of regular expressions in
watt.client.oauth.allowlist.allowedServers sequentially for every request.
Integration Server performs a regular expression match operation on each regular
expression until a match is found or all regular expressions in the list have
been evaluated. Place the more frequently matched regular expressions at the
beginning of the comma-separated list. 

Note: If the watt.client.oauth.allowlist.enabled parameter is set to true and
you do not specify a value for watt.client.oauth.allowlist.allowedServers, all
calls to pub.client.oauth:executeRequest end with an error. 

Important!  If your solution uses the pub.client.oauth:executeRequest service,
after applying a fix that includes PIE-98917 you must take one of the following
actions: 
- Disable the use of an allow list with pub.client.oauth:executeRequest by
setting watt.client.oauth.allowlist.enabled to false. 
- Specify a list of allowed URIs in the
watt.client.oauth.allowlist.allowedServers parameter.

PIE-99563 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix22)
When Integration Server is configured to write server log messages at the TRACE
level, the server log does not mask data from the Authorization header. 

If a request uses an authorization scheme beside Bearer or Basic and Integration
Server is configured to write log messages at the TRACE level, the server log
includes the raw bytes of the Authorization header. This poses a security
vulnerability. 

Now, Integration Server masks the contents of the Authorization header in log
messages. 

PIE-99592 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix22)
The Eclipse JGit library included with Integration Server has been upgraded.

For Integration Server 11.1 the JGit library has been upgraded to version 7.3.0
from version 6.7.0. 
For Integration Server 10.15, the JGit library has been upgraded to version
6.10.1 from version 6.7.0. 

Upgrading the JGit library resolves the following security vulnerability:
CVE-2025-4949. 

PIE-99717 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix22)
PATCH requests lose their request bodies when redirected with 307 or 308
responses. 

Integration Server does not preserve request bodies for the PATCH method during
307 (Temporary Redirect) or 308 (Permanent Redirect) responses. As a result, it
sends redirected requests without the original payload, leading to incomplete or
invalid updates on the target endpoint. This behavior causes integration failures,
data inconsistencies, and unexpected errors—particularly in environments with
frequent redirects where the redirected endpoint depends on the PATCH request
body. 

This issue is now resolved. Redirect handling is enhanced to ensure that
PATCH requests retain and forward their original request body when the HTTP
client request includes a valid the Location header, the followRedirect
parameter is enabled, and the response status code is 307 or 308. This ensures 
reliable and standards-compliant redirect behavior.

PIE-88551 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix21)
The webMethods messaging triggers fail with the following error during document
processing:

“[ISS.0153.0041E] webMethods Messaging Trigger <Trigger_name> failed
preprocessing: java.lang.NullPointerException”

When a webMethods messaging trigger receives a document without an attached
envelope for document processing, Integration Server throws NullPointerException
because of the missing envelope. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-96908 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix21)
The pub.string:messageFormat service fails to process patterns that contain
double quotes.

When you provide a pattern with double quotes as input to the service,
for example, “{1}” <some_text>, the service execution fails.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-97669 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix21)
Integration Server does not decode the password provided by the JDBC pool
configuration properly. 

If the password for JDBC pool configuration is provided directly rather than
saved in the outbound password file, Integration Server decodes the password
incorrectly. As a result, when the password is supplied to the JDBC pool, the
password is incorrect and might include invalid characters. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-97764 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix21)
Integration Server accepts HTTP requests with invalid or empty Host headers
without validation, creating potential vulnerabilities.
 
Integration Server does not validate the incoming HTTP requests and responds
with the 200 OK status code even when the Host header is missing or invalid,
allowing arbitrary host values and exposing the server to security risks.
 
This issue is now resolved by introducing a new server configuration parameter,
watt.server.security.allowedHostHeaders.
 
watt.server.security.allowedHostHeaders:
Specifies a comma-separated list of valid Host header values that Integration
Server accepts for incoming HTTP requests. When you set the
parameter, Integration Server validates the Host header in incoming requests
and returns an "Invalid Host Header" message if the value is not included in
the list or the Host header is left empty. The parameter also supports the
wildcard character asterisk (*) for pattern matching.
For example, watt.server.security.allowedHostHeaders=*.example.com:5555
allows 123.example.com:5555 and abc.example.com:5555 but rejects 
example.com:5555. If you do not set this parameter, Integration Server 
continues to accept all values without validation.
Note: If you set an incorrect hostname or omit the port of the 
Integration Server instance in the parameter value, you may get locked out of 
Integration Server Administrator with an Invalid Host Header error. To avoid 
getting locked out, always include the hostname and port of the 
Integration Server instance in the parameter. If you get locked out, access 
Integration Server Administrator using the server IP and port, then update the 
parameter with the correct values.

You do not need to restart Integration Server for changes to this parameter to
take effect.

PIE-97960 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix21)
Integration Server Administrator fails to load the home page of a custom
package. 

Generating package documentation for a custom package from Designer completes
successfully. However, Integration Server Administrator becomes unresponsive
while loading the home page for the same custom package.

PIE-97963 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix21)
Integration Server throws com.wm.app.b2b.server.ServiceException:

PIE-97971 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix21)
Integration Server omits response body due to mismatch between the response 
media type and the OpenAPI definition.

In OpenAPI specification, response schemas are defined per status code and media 
type. If the response media type includes wildcards or parameters
(application/json; charset=utf-8), the server may not return the body. The body
is returned only when the media type exactly matches the OpenAPI definition.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-98034 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix21)
Certified container images for Integration Server and Microservices Runtime now
use standard base images. 

Prior to this fix, certified container images for Integration Server and
Microservices Runtime used a customized base image of UBI or Alpine. Now, the
certified container images use the standard base images available for UBI and
Alpine. 

Integration Server images use Red Hat Universal Base Image 9 Minimal
(ubi9-minimal). 

Microservices Runtime images are provided with ubi9-minimal or the standard
Alpine with a musl JDK, such as azul/zulu-openjdk-alpine:17-latest. 

PIE-98083 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix21)

minute intervals. However, the utility generates logs more frequently, resulting

PIE-98219 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix21)
Creating signed S/MIME data using the pub.smime.keystore:createSignedData

PIE-98290 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix21)
Enhancements to statistics data collection.

Integration Server introduces the following changes to provide more control of 
collection of purging and data by the Statistics Data Collector.

- A configuration parameter to disable persistence of time-series data.
The Statistics Data Collector can be configured to capture data statistics for 
time-series data but not save that data to a database. A call to the /metrics 
endpoint returns time-series data for the current time period. However, the 
Dashboard does not display time-series data for the JVM metrics, Usages, 
Services, or APIs tabs.
Use the watt.server.statisticsDataCollector.includeTimeSeriesData server 
configuration parameter to control whether the Statistics Data Collector persists 
time-series data. Set watt.server.statisticsDataCollector.includeTimeSeriesData 
to true to collect and persist time-series data. Set the parameter to false to 
collect but not time persist time-series data. Integration Server does not need 
to be restarted for changes to this parameter to take effect. The default value 
is true.

- A configuration parameter to control the frequency with which the Statistics 
Data Collector deletes old data.
The Statistics Data Collector deletes old data in batches using a scheduled 
system task that runs every 4 hours. (Note this is a JVM system task, not an 
Integration Server system task). For every scheduled delete task, Statistics 
Data Collector deletes the batches of data collected over a 4 hour period 
starting with the oldest data. The delete task performs batch deletions every 
30 seconds until all data older than the retention date is removed. The 
retention date is controlled by the retentionDays parameter. Prior to this fix, 
the frequency of the system task could not be changed. Now, Integration Server 
includes server configuration parameters to control the frequency with which the 
Statistics Data Collector purges data and the amount of data purged in each deletion.

watt.server.statisticsDataCollector.removal.interval specifies the number of 
hours between each purge of data by the Statistics Data Collector. Set this 
parameter to a value greater than or equal to 0. The default is 4 hours. If the 
parameter is set to 0, the Statistics Data Collector does not manage the removal 
of data. The user must manage deletion of statistics data.

Integration Server must be restarted for changes to this parameter to take effect.

Note: The watt.server.statisticsDataCollector.includeTimeSeriesData value does 
not impact whether the Statistics Data Collector deletes old data. If you disable 
persistence of time-series data, the Statics Data Collector still removes stale 
data with a JVM system task. This behavior allows the purge to run without 
collecting any additional data.

watt.server.statisticsDataCollector.removal.rows specifies a time interval that 
determines the number of rows that each purge removes from the database. To 
reduce pressure on the database server, the Statistics Data Collector removes 
stale data for the specified segment of time. For example, a value of 15m 
indicates that each deleted batch encompasses data collected in a 15 minute time 
period. Specify 1 to 3 integers followed by the letters h, H, m, M to indicate 
whether the unit of time is in minutes or hours. The default is 4 hours. If you 
do not include a unit of time, the Statistics Data Colector ignore the provided 
value and uses the default of 4 hours.

Integration Server does not need to be restarted for changes to this parameter 
to take effect.

- An internal service to provide more information about the Statistics Data 
Collector, including values of server configuration parameters. Use the following 
URL to obtain status information: <http://host:port>/invoke/wm.server.datacollector:status

PIE-98311 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix20)

request with a large payload using chunked transfer encoding.

When a REST API uses the pub.client:http service to send a large payload in a
POST request in chunks, the configured flow timeout is not honored. This issue
occurs because sending the payload in chunks causes the request to take longer
time to complete. During this process, the flow timeout is not enforced as
expected. Consequently, the request continues beyond the configured limit and
eventually fails with an HTTP 500 error after a significant delay.

PIE-95103 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix19)
Support for using environment variables or a new custom_setenv.(bat,sh) file to 
add classes or libraries to the beginning or end of the Microservices Runtime 
classpath instead of modifying setenv.(bat,sh) .
 
Previously, to add classes or libraries to the beginning or end of the server 
classpath for Microservices Runtime, users needed to add the full path in the 
Java system properties PREPENDCLASSES or APPENDCLASSES in the 
<Integration Server_directory>/bin/setenv.(bat,sh) file. Similarly, users needed 
to set the Java system property PREPEND_SYSTEM_CLASSPATH to add classes or 
libraries to the beginning of the Java classpath and set APPEND_SYSTEM_CLASSPATH 
to add classes or libraries to the end of the Java classpath. Further, the 
setenv.(bat,sh) file can be overwritten as part of applying a fix to Integration 
Server. As a result, the configuration requirement to update sentenv.(bat,sh) is 
inflexible and may be difficult to maintain in a containerized environment.
 
To address this issue, Microservices Runtime introduces the following changes 
for adding classes and libraries to the server or system classpath:
• A custom_setenv.(bat,sh) file which supports additions to the classpath through 
the PREPENDCLASSES, APPENDCLASSES, PREPEND_SYSTEM_CLASSPATH, APPEND_SYSTEM_CLASSPATH 
properties in the file.
• Environment variables that can be supplied during Microservices Runtime startup 
to specify additions to the classpath: ENV_PREPENDCLASSES, ENV_APPENDCLASSES, 
ENV_PREPEND_SYSTEM_CLASSPATH, and ENV_APPEND_SYSTEM_CLASSPATH.
 
After applying this fix, take the following steps to add classes and libraries 
can be added to the server classpath and the Java classpath:
1. If you previously specified values for one or more of the following properties 
   in setenv.(bat,sh) file, use a text editor to remove the parameters from the 
   file: PREPENDCLASSES, APPENDCLASSES, PREPEND_SYSTEM_CLASSPATH, APPEND_SYSTEM_CLASSPATH
2. To add classes or libraries to the server or Java classpath using the 
   custom_setenv.(bat,sh) file, use a text editor to open 
   <Integration Server_directory>{}/bin/ custom_setenv.(bat,sh) and set one or 
   more of the following parameters and then save the file:
   PREPENDCLASSES - classes or libraries to add to the beginning of the server 
   classpath for Microservices Runtime
   APPENDCLASSES - classes or libraries to add to the end of the server classpath 
   for Microservices Runtime
   PREPEND_SYSTEM_CLASSPATH - classes or libraries to add to the beginning of 
   the Java classpath for Microservices Runtime
   APPEND_SYSTEM_CLASSPATH - classes or libraries to add to the end of the Java 
   classpath for Microservices Runtime
3. To add classes or libraries to the server or Java classpath by supplying 
   environment variables, set one or more of the following environment variables 
   when starting Microservice Runtime:
   ENV_PREPENDCLASSES - classes or libraries to add to the beginning of the server 
   classpath for Microservices Runtime
   ENV_APPENDCLASSES - classes or libraries to add to the end of the server 
   classpath for Microservices Runtime
   ENV_PREPEND_SYSTEM_CLASSPATH - classes or libraries to add to the beginning 
   of the Java classpath for Microservices Runtime
   ENV_APPEND_SYSTEM_CLASSPATH - classes or libraries to add to the end of the 
   Java classpath for Microservices Runtime

Note: If a value is set for a property in custom_setenv.(bat,sh) and for the 
corresponding environment variable, the environment variable takes precedence.

Important! After applying a fix that includes PIE-95103 and moving 
PREPENDCLASSES, APPENDCLASSES, PREPEND_SYSTEM_CLASSPATH, APPEND_SYSTEM_CLASSPATH 
from setenv.(bat,sh) to custom_setenv.(bat,sh), do not edit setenv.(bat,sh).

PIE-96394 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix19)
When using webmethods.io, the jsonStringToDocument public service fails to parse 
multi-dimensional JSON arrays.

Invoking the jsonStringToDocument service over HTTP returns an illegal character 
error message and the service cannot parse the multi-dimensional JSON array.

PIE-96988 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix19)
Support for using the acr_values parameter in an authorization request sent to 
the Open ID Provider from Integration Server.

When sending an authorization request to an Open ID Provider, Integration Sever 
includes acr_values parameter which specifies acr (Authentication Context Class 
Reference) values set in the OpenID JSON configuration file. Integration Server 
sets values for the acr_values request parameter using the following logic:

- If the OpenID configuration file includes the acr_values and 
acr_values_supported parameters, Integration Server validates the contents of 
acr_values against the acr_values_supported. Integration Server adds only the 
acr values that appear in the acr_values_supported to the acr_values parameter 
in the authorization request.

- If the OpenID configuration file includes acr_values only, Integration Server 
adds the acr values to the acr_values parameter in the authorization request.

 The configuration file is at the following location: 
 <IntegrationServer>\instances\<instanceName>\config\security\openid

PIE-96333 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix19)
The namespace advanced search service makes Integration Server
vulnerable to ReDoS attacks.

The namespace advanced search service allows regex-based searches without
validation or timeout, making Integration Server vulnerable to ReDoS attacks.

This issue is now resolved by adding a timeout parameter to the service.
When the timeout parameter is set, Integration Server uses Java regular
expressions only regardless of the configured regex engine. If the
parameter is not set, the configured regex engine (Perl5 or Java Regex)
is used. By default, the parameter value is blank.

PIE-96614 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix19)
Integration Server throws NullPointerException when an external client calls a 
service immediately after a flow timeout.

When an external API client, such as Postman, sends a request to a service with 
a configured flow timeout, Integration Server throws NullPointerException if the 
client immediately makes a subsequent call after the service experiences a 
thread interruption due to the timeout. This issue occurs when the 
watt.server.threadKill.interruptThread.enabled server configuration parameter
is set to true.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-96648 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix19)
The pub.client:http service ignores the flow timeout when it fails to establish
a connection.

When a flow service uses an Invoke step to call the pub.client:http service but 
fails to establish a connection, the service waits for the full connection 
timeout to expire before retrying, ignoring the flow timeout. The service should 
consider both the flow timeout and connection timeout and adjust connection 
retries accordingly. However, the service fails to adjust the connection timeout 
or retries based on the flow timeout, causing inconsistencies.

This issue is now resolved. Now, the service honors the flow timeout.

the "Access Denied. Invalid CSRF Secure Token" message.

This issue is resolved. Now, the user is redirected to the dashboard,
bypassing the login page.

PIE-96601 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix19)
Support for additional JNDI provider alias properties in configuration variables 
templates.

The following JNDI configuration properties can now be used with a configuration 
variables template (application.properties):

- Description: jndi.<aliasName>.description        
- Truststore Alias: jndi.<aliasName>.trustStoreAlias       
- Keystore Alias: jndi.<aliasName>.keyStoreAlias     
- Key Alias: jndi.<aliasName>.keyAlias    
- Truststore Property Name: jndi.<aliasName>.trustStoreProp    
- Truststore Password Property Name: jndi.<aliasName>.trustStorePwdProp      
- Keystore Property Name: jndi.<aliasName>.keyStoreProp        
- Keystore Password Property Name:  jndi.<aliasName>.keyStorePwdProp          
- Keystore Format Property Name: jndi.<aliasName>.keyStoreFormatProp         
- Private Key Property Name: jndi.<aliasName>.privateKeyProp 
- Other Properties: jndi.<aliasName>.<otherProp1>=<value1>

Other Properties are properties the JNDI provider requires for JNDI configuration 
that do not correspond to a JNDI provider alias property. For each additional 
property, add  jndi.<aliasName>.<otherProp1>=<value1>  where <otherProp> is the 
property name and <value1> is the property value.

PIE-96368 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix19)

to Regular Expression Denial of Service (ReDoS) attacks.

The pub.string:lookupTable service allows regex-based searches without
validation or timeout, making Integration Server vulnerable to
ReDoS attacks.

This issue is now resolved by adding the regexTimeout input parameter to 
the service.

regexTimeout: Specifies the maximum execution time in milliseconds for regex 
matching. Integration Server supports the Perl5 (Apache ORO) and Java Regex 
engines for regex matching. When regexTimeout is set, Integration Server uses 
Java Regex regardless of the configured regex engine. If not set, the configured 
regex engine (Perl5 or Java Regex) is used. By default, the parameter value is blank.

PIE-93828 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix19)
New option to prevent using credentials for a confidential OAuth client to 
execute services.
 
When registering an OAuth client of type confidential, Integration Server 
creates a user account and shares a client secret for the account with the 
administrator who registered the client. The client secret and client ID are the 
credentials the confidential client needs to complete activities such as 
requesting an access token and refreshing an access token. However, by default, 
Integration Server does not restrict the client from using the credentials to 
invoke other services.
 
Integration Server now provides a server configuration parameter that you can 
use to restrict the use of client ID and client secret to services handling OAuth 
requests only.
 
watt.server.oauth.restrictCredentials
Specifies whether Integration Server restricts the use of credentials for a 
confidential OAuth client to services that handle OAuth requests only. When set 
to false, the client ID and client secret for a registered confidential client 
can be used to invoke any service on Integration Server. When set to true, 
attempts to use the credentials for a confidential client to invoke a service 
that does not handle OAuth processing results in a rejection of the request. The 
default is false.
 
You do not need to restart Integration server for changes to this parameter to 
take effect.

PIE-94184 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix19)
Single sign-on to Integration Server Administrator using SAML.

Integration Server now provides single sign-on (SSO) for Integration Server 
Administrator using SAML 2.0. 
In the SAML single sign-on process, Integration Server acts as the service 
provider and sends a SAML request to the Identity Provider (IdP). The IdP 
authenticates the user and sends a SAML response to Integration Server. 
Integration Server validates the signature of the SAML response and then logs 
identified user into Integration Server Administrator. 

After applying this fix, you must complete the following tasks to configure 
SAML-based SSO for Integration Server Administrator:

Complete the following prerequisites:

- Configure an identity provider (IdP) for use with Integration Server. 
  Activities include creating a profile for Integration Server in the IdP and 
  creating a client ID for the profile. 

- Work with the IdP administrator to configure signing and encryption keys for 
  the SAML response.

To configure SAML-based SSO for Integration Server Administrator: 

1. Create a new configuration file named samlsso.cnf with the entries provided 
   in the section “samlsso.cnf configuration file”, below. 

   Replace the sample values with values specific to your environment.  

2. Save the samlsso.cnf file in the following location:
   <webm_install_dir>/IntegrationServer/instances/<instance-name>/config/security/saml 

3 Restart Integration Server.

4. Using Integration Server Administrator, define a trusted SAML issuer for the IdP.
   Navigate to the Security > SAML page and click Add SAML Token Issuer.
   Supply the following information:   

   - Issuer Name: the idpURL value in the samlsso.cnf configuration file.

   - Truststore Alias: Alias to the truststore that contains the public keys of 
     the SAML token issuer.

   - Certificate Alias: The alias within the truststore that contains the public 
     key of the SAML token issuer. Integration Server uses this certificate 
	 associated with this key to verify the signature of the SAML Response 
	 returned by the IdP.


samlsso.cnf configuration file
The samlsso.cnf configuration file contains the configuration that Integration 
Server needs to send SAML requests and handle SAML assertions in responses. The 
samlsso.cnf file must contain the following entries with the sample value 
replaced by values specific to your environment:

samlsso.enabled=true
samlsso.idpUrl=http://idpHost:8080/realms/samlsso/protocol/saml
samlsso.acsUrl=http://IShost:5555/WmAdmin?samlsso=true
samlsso.issuerId=http://IShost:5555/WmAdmin?samlsso=true
samlsso.signRequest=true
samlsso.keystoreAlias=is_keystore
samlsso.signatureKeyAlias=keycloak
samlsso.encryptionKeyAlias=keycloak
samlsso.groupAttribute=Groups
samlsso.groupMappings.1.from=admins
samlsso.groupMappings.1.to=Administrators,Developers,ReadOnlyAdministrators
samlsso.groupMappings.2.from=everyone
samlsso.groupMappings.2.to=Everybody

enabled - true|false. Whether SAML-based SSO is in use for this Integration Server.
          Must be set to true for SAML-based SSO to work. 

idpURL - URL to which Integration Server sends the SAML request for authentication.

acsURL - URL of the assertion consumer, which is Integration Server.
         The identity provider (IdP) redirects to this URL with the SAML response.
         Replace ISHost with the host name or IP addresses of Integration Server.
         Replace 5555 with a secure port on Integration Server. 

issuerId - Client ID of the profile defined for Integration Server in the IdP. 

signRequest - true|false. Whether to sign the SAML request that Integration Server 
              sends to the IdP.
              Set to true if the IdP accepts signed SAML requests. 

keystoreAlias - Integration Server keystore alias that contains the certificates 
                for signing
                SAML requests and decrypting the SAML response returned from the 
				IdP.

signatureKeyAlias - Key alias for the certificate to use for signing the SAML 
                    request.

encryptionKeyAlias - Key alias for the certificate to use for decrypting a SAML 
                     response from the IdP. 

groupAttribute - Name of the IdP attribute that contains the group membership of 
                 the user. Integration Server scans the SAML assertion and looks 
				 for a SAML Attribute by this name. Integration Server uses the 
				 values for performing mappings from IdP groups to Integration 
				 Server groups. 

groupMappings - An array to map IdP groups to Integration Server groups.
                For example, the first one shows that, if the value of 
				groupAttribute contains "admins", it is mapped to the Integration 
				Server group named Administrators, Developers, and 
				ReadOnlyAdministrators. Because the Administrators group is part 
				of Administrators ACL, this user will be able to log into 
				Integration Server Administrator.


For each IdP group that needs to be mapped to one or more groups in Integration 
Server, create a pair of group mapping entries that start with the format 
samlsso.groupMappings.# where # is a number. One member of the pair must include 
“from” in the entry name and the other member must include “to”. For example:

samlsso.groupMappings.1.from
samlsso.groupMappings.1.to

Use the samlsso.groupMappings.#.from entry to specify the IdP group that you to 
map to the Integration Server user groups in the samlsso.groupMappings.#.to entry. 

For example, the entries below establish group mapping 1 in which a user that 
belongs to the IdP group named admins will be a member of the Integration Server 
groups Administrators, Developers and ReadOnlyAdministrators.

samlsso.groupMappings.1.from=admins
samlsso.groupMappings.1.to=Administrators,Developers,ReadOnlyAdministrators

The entries below establish group mapping 2 in which a user that belongs to IdP 
group "everyone" will be a member of the "Everybody" user group in Integration 
Server.

samlsso.groupMappings.2.from=everyone
samlsso.groupMappings.2.to=Everybody

For SAML-based SSO for Integration Server Administrator to work, Administrators 
must be one of the groups listed for “to”.
The membership of the user in the Integration Server user group is temporary and 
does not persist across server restarts. 

When processing the SAML-based SSO assertion, Integration Server first checks to 
see if the user identified in the NameID of the SAML assertion exists on 
Integration Server. Integration Server searches users defined locally and then 
users defined external (LDAP or Central Users). If the user exists, Integration 
Server ignores the groupAttribute and groupMappings entries.
If the user does not exist, Integration Server creates a temporary user with a 
name that matches the NameID from the assertion. Integration Server then extracts 
the groupAttribute value to map the user to groups as defined in the groupMappings 
entry in the configuration file.

Temporary users remain in Integration Server memory until Integration Server 
shuts down.

After configuring SSO, a user can log into Integration Server Administrator by 
clicking “Log in with single sign on” on the https://<host>:<port> login page.

PIE-97437 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix19)
Changes to the internal methods that Integration Server uses for the cache that 
stores OAuth authorization codes to support API Gateway.

PIE-97417 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix19)
After applying a fix that includes PIE-94420, Integration Server may incorrectly 
enable metering for an Integration Server with a core-based license.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-95838 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix19)
Option to roll back the pipeline when a TRY step ends with failure.

When a TRY step ends with failure, Integration Server does not roll back the 
pipeline to the state that existed immediately prior to TRY step execution. 
Instead, the pipeline contains any changes made by the TRY step. Legacy try-catch 
behavior built using SEQUENCE steps does result in rollback of the pipeline if the 
SEQUENCE step ends with failure.

To resolve the behavior inconsistency between the TRY steps and the legacy 
try-catch behavior provided via SEQEUNCE, Integration Server now includes a 
server configuration parameter that can be set to determine if Integration Server 
rolls back the pipeline when an error occurs during the TRY step.

watt.server.flow.tryStep.restorePipelineOnError

Specifies whether Integration Server rolls back the pipeline when an error that 
occurs during execution of a TRY step results in failure of the TRY step. When 
set to true, if an error occurs within the TRY step that causes the TRY step to 
end in failure, Integration Server rolls back the pipeline to the state prior to 
TRY step execution. When set to false, Integration Server does not roll back the 
pipeline if an error results in failure of the TRY step. The default value is false.

Integration Server needs to be restarted for changes to the parameter to take 
effect.

Note: Rollback operations are performed on the ﬁrst level of the pipeline only. 
That is, ﬁrst-level variables are restored to their original values before the 
step failed, but Integration Server does not roll back changes to any documents 
to which the ﬁrst-level variables refer.

PIE-94563 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix19)
Integration Server does not clear forwardable headers after processing a request, 
resulting in re-use of the headers in subsequent requests.

Integration Server now clears forwardable headers after processing a request.
