PIE-81364 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix9)
Integration Server now includes options to control how Java lists and sets are
encoded in a JSON string. 

When Integration Server encodes a document (IData) as a JSON string, such as in
the built-in service pub.json:documentToJSONString), Integration Server encodes
an instance of java.util.List or java.util.Set as one String value. However,
this data would be more properly encoded as an array. 

To resolve this issue, Integration Server now includes the following to control
how instances of java.util.List and java.util.Set are encoded in a JSON string: 

The server configuration parameter watt.server.json.encodeListsAndSetsAsArrays
determines the encoding at a server-wide level. 
The input parameter encodeListsAndSetsAsArrays for the
pub.json:documentToJSONString service determines the encoding per service
invocation. 

Details about these parameters appear below.

watt.server.json.encodeListsAndSetsAsArrays
Specifies how Integration Server encodes instances of java.util.List and
java.util.Set when converting a document (IData) to a JSON string. Set to true
to encode instances of java.util.List or java.util.Set as arrays. Set to false
to encode instances of java.util.List or java.util.Set as one String value. The
default is false. 

You do not need to restart Integration Server for changes to this parameter to
take effect. 

pub.json:documentToJSONString
encodeListsAndSetsAsArrays - String. Optional. Specifies how the
pub.json:documentToJSONString service encodes instances of java.util.List or
java.util.Set. 

Set to one of the following:
- "true" to encode instances of java.util.List or java.util.Set as arrays.
- "false" to encode instances of java.util.List and java.util.Set as one
String value. 
- <null> to use the value of watt.server.json.encodeListsAndSetsAsArrays to
determine the encoding. 
There is no default value for this input parameter.

PIE-82233 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix9)
Integration Server now includes the ability to control wither it encodes a
java.util.Map object as a JSON string or a nested JSON structure. 

When encoding IData objects as JSON, Integration Server encodes java.util.Map
objects as a JSON string instead of a nested JSON structure. To address this,
Integration Server now includes the following to determine the encoding: 

- The server configuration parameter watt.server.json.encodeMapAsString
determines the encoding at a server-wide level. 
- The input parameter encodeMapAsString in the pub.json:documentToJSONString
service determines the encoding on a per service invocation basis. 

Details about these parameters appear below.

watt.server.json.encodeMapAsString
Specifies how Integration Server encodes java.util.Map objects in JSON. Set to
true to encode Map objects as a JSON string. Set to false to encode Map objects
as a nested JSON structure. The default is true. 

For example, in the following suppose that "myKey" is an IData key with a
HashMap value that has two String keys each with a numeric value. 

"myKey" ->   "one" = 1,  "two" = 2

A value of true results in this JSON:   "myKey": "{one=2, two=1}"
A value of false results in this JSON:   "myKey" : { "one" : 1, "two" : 2 }  

Integration Server does not need to be restarted for changes to this parameter
to take effect. 

pub.json:documentToJSONString 
encodeMapAsString - String. Optional. Specifies how the service encodes
java.util.Map objects in the document (IData). 
Set to one of the following:

- "true" to encode java.util.Map objects as a JSON string
- "false" to encode java.util.Map objects as a nested JSON structure.
- <null> to use the value of watt.server.json.encodeMapAsString to determine the
encoding. 

PIE-84869 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix9)
Integration Server has scheduler issues in quiesce mode.

Consider a scheduled task that is active when Integration Server enters quiesce
mode. If the scheduled task is updated in quiesce mode, Integration Server
suspends the task. Upon exiting quiesce mode, the task remains suspended. 

This issue is resolved. Now, tasks that are active before Integration Server 
enters quiesce mode will remain active when Integration Server exits quiesce 
mode.

Additionally, when Integration Server enters quiesce mode, the order of
package unloading is changed. Integration Server now unloads custom packages
before system packages, regardless of the package dependencies defined for the
custom packages. 

PIE-84943 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix9)
When a client uses an invalid or expired OAuth access token, Integration Server
always responds with HTML instead of the media type specified in the Accept
header of the request. 

This has been resolved. Now, when the client uses an invalid or expired access
token, Integration Server uses the media type requested by the Accept header to
send the error response. If the request did not include an Accept header, the
media type of the response matches the media type of the request. 

PIE-85568 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix9)
An accumulation of unused breakpoint sessions might negatively impact
Integration Server performance. 

Using Designer to execute a service in debug mode creates a breakpoint session
on Integration Server. However, breakpoint sessions do not expire and
Integration Server does not remove idle sessions. This can result in an
accumulation of breakpoint sessions on Integration Server, which can affect
Integration Server performance. 

To resolve this issue, breakpoint sessions now expire and Integration Server
includes the system task Expired Breakpoint Session Sweeper which removes
expired breakpoint sessions. Integration Server includes two new server
configuration parameters to control the expiry time and the interval with which
the system task runs. 
 
watt.server.breakpoint.session.expiryTime 
Specifies the number of minutes a breakpoint session can be idle before it
expires. A breakpoint session is created when Designer executes a service in
debug mode. The default is 30. 

You must restart Integration Server for changes to this parameter to take
effect. 

watt.server.breakpoint.session.sweeperInterval
Specifies the number of minutes between execution of the system task Expired
Breakpoint Session Sweeper which removes expired breakpoint sessions. The
default is 15 minutes. 

You must restart Integration Server for changes to this parameter to take
effect. 

PIE-85574 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix9)
A JMS trigger does not work as expected when using Universal Messaging as the
messaging provider, and the 'Max prefetch size' property is greater than one.

When the JMS trigger receives messages from Universal Messaging, the "Max
prefetch size" property in the JMS trigger overrides the "Max batch messages"
property.

This issue is resolved. Now, when the "Max batch messages" property is greater
than one, Integration Server honors the property, and ignores the "Max prefetch
size" property.

The JMS trigger uses the prefetch cache only in the following scenarios:

- The JMS trigger uses concurrent processing. However, serial JMS triggers
 that receive messages from Universal Messaging cannot use prefetch caching.
- The JMS connection alias that the trigger uses to fetch messages has
the transaction type set to NO_TRANSACTION.
- The JMS trigger receives messages from multiple destinations, and the number of
destinations matches the value set for the "Connection count" property.
- The "Max prefetch size" property of the JMS trigger is greater than one.
- The "Max batch messages" property of the JMS trigger is less than two. 

PIE-85634 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix9)
Integration Server sets the HPROXY and HAUTH system properties to configure the
proxy host and port while connecting to webMethods Cloud. 
However, the HPROXY property does not align with other proxy 
settings, resulting in connection failures.

This issue is resolved. Now, Integration Server only sets the HAUTH system
property using watt.net.proxy.proxyAlias. However, if the HPROXY property is
already available in the server.cnf file, remove the property manually. 
If watt.net.proxy.proxyAlias is not set and a default proxy is configured,
Integration Server still sets the HAUTH system property according to the default
proxy configuration. 

Additionally, Integration Server now defines the "http.nonProxyHosts" system
property using the values set for the watt.net.proxySkipList property. 
For example, if watt.net.proxySkipList is localhost, host.example.com, 
Integration Server sets the http.nonProxyHosts value as
localhost|host.example.com 

PIE-85647 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix9)
Attempt to refresh an expired access token results in a NullPointerException.

If the foreign key constraint from the IS_OAUTH_REFRESHTOKEN table to the
IS_OAUTH_TOKEN table is removed, a NullPointerException can occur while
attempting to refresh an access token that has expired. 

This fix adds additional protections to prevent a NullPointerException in this
scenario. Instead, Integration Server will respond with a 400 status code and an
error message. 

Important! Software AG does not recommended modifying database constraints
unless directed to do so by Software AG Global Support. 

PIE-85662 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix9)
Multiple concurrently running instances of the Remove Expired Tokens system task
might cause Integration Server to become unresponsive. 

An instance of the scheduled system task Remove Expired Tokens can run before
the previous instance completes, resulting in multiple executions running
concurrently. Over time, this might cause Integration Server to become
unresponsive. 

Now, Integration Server does not start a new instance of the Remove Expired
Tokens task until the currently executing instance completes and the interval
specified in watt.server.oauth.token.removal.interval elapses. 

PIE-85912 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix9)
Integration Server incorrectly decodes encoded French/Latin characters in a
request header. As a result, the response sent to the client API Gateway
displays the French/Latin characters as question marks. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-86107 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix9)
Migrating Integration Server from 10.11 to 10.15 results in blank
values for "Global variables". 
 
When migrating from 10.11 to the latest version, if the imported 
ACDL file contains a global variable name with a "." character, Integration 
Server considers the global variable as a package variable, leading to blank 
values for the global variable.
With the introduction of package variables in Integration Server 10.15, package 
variables names are in the <<pkgname.varname>> format. Therefore, in the ACDL 
file generated in 10.15, Integration Server substitutes the "." character 
with ".." to prevent ambiguity. As a result, ACDL files created in earlier 
versions that do not support package variables fail to function as expected. 

This issue is now resolved by extending support to ensure compatibility with
earlier versions.

PIE-86121 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix9)
Integration Server does not support the built-in pub.security services in the
FIPS mode. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-86143 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix9)
LDAP and CDS groups can be assigned to allow or deny lists for ACLs (Access
Control Lists) using a configuration variables template. 

Previously, only local groups could be assigned to the allow or deny lists for
ACLs using a configuration variables template (application.properties). Groups
defined in LDAP and CDS (Common Directory Services), which are external
directories could not be assigned to ACLs using a configuration variables
template. This was limiting. 

Now, LDAP and CDS groups can be assigned to allow or deny lists for ACLs (Access
Control Lists) using a configuration variables template. To add groups defined
in LDAP or CDS to the allow or deny list for an ACL, add the prefix "ldap/"
or "cds/" followed by the group name. For example, the following key=value
pair adds the LDAP user myLdapUser and the CDS user myCentralUser to the allow
list for the Administrators ACL: 

acl.Administrators.allow=ldap/myLdapUser, cds/myCentralUser

Note: Local groups can include the "local/" prefix with the group name but
do not have to. 

In addition to the above changes, a configuration variables template can now be
used to add LDAP groups directly to the LDAP configuration file. The LDAP Group
asset supports a single key named ldapgroup.<groupName>.dn which corresponds to
the distinguished name of the group. The <groupName> is the alias that
Integration Server will use to store information about the LDAP group once it is
created by applying the template. 

For example:
ldapgroup.myGroupName.dn=cn\=generalgroup,ou\=company,dc\=example,dc\=com 

The above example includes backslashes () to escape equal signs.

PIE-86233 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix9)
A rule violation alert email generated for the Denial of Service

When you enable the Denial of Service by IP policy, the rule violation alert 
email for a request in the Enterprise Gateway Server shows the load balancer

watt.server.enterprisegateway.ignoreXForwardedForHeader server configuration

input pipeline of the gRPC method flow service. 

In gRPC, fields have type-specific default values. When a gRPC request included
one or more fields set to the default for the field type, Integration Server did
not include the value in the data passed to the input pipeline of the gRPC
method flow service. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-72571 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Integration Server generates a TCP RST (reset) signal when closing an outbound
socket connection. 

Now, Integration Sever no longer generates a TCP RST signal when closing
outbound socket connections. 

PIE-79558 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)

From Integration Server 10.11, exchanging SOAP messages using the 
Web Services Reliable Messaging protocol leads to increased error logging in 
the wrapper.log file.

This issue is resolved. Now, Integration Server logs the errors only when 
you set the Web Service stack facility (0141) to "Debug" in Integration Server 
Administrator > Logs > Logging configuration > Server Logger > Edit Server
Logger. 

PIE-80586 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Integration Server returns the following exception for a SOAP request
with payload exceeding 1MB: 
"Exception parsing native service provider com.ctc.wstx.exc.WstxEOFException:
Unexpected EOF in attribute value".

Integration Server returns the exception for a SOAP request with payload
exceeding 1MB because the "enableSoapValidation" parameter in the Axis2 
configuration file is set to true by default, preventing Axis2 from parsing the 
incoming SOAP request.

This issue is resolved. Now, by default, the "enableSoapValidation" parameter is 
set to false.

result in package corruption. 

This issue is resolved now. Packages are now loaded in order during
repository-based deployment.

PIE-81510 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Outlook cannot open emails encrypted and sent by Integration Server.

If the pub.smime:createEncryptedData service is used to encrypt a MIME message
which is then sent using the pub.client:smtp service, Outlook receives the
message but cannot read it. Outlook might display the following message:
"Cannot open this item. A private key to decrypt the document is missing!"
This issue occurs because the pub.smime:createEncryptedData service creates a
MIME message that cannot be decrypted by Outlook. Specifically the MIME message
created by the service includes an extra line between headers. 

The pub.smime:createEncryptedData service no longer includes the extra line
between headers, allowing the MIME message to be decrypted by Outlook.

tn.BigDocThreshold property, Integration Server treats the data as large without 
honoring the watt.server.mime.largeDataThreshold parameter.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-82866 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
When Integration Server executes pub.client.ftp:login and

sends two ClientHello requests to the remote FTPS server during the handshake
instead of one because Integration Server was attempting hostname verification

PIE-83129 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)

PIE-83252 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
The pub.smime.keystore:processEncryptedData service fails to decrypt the S/MIME
stream encrypted in Integration Server 10.5 or earlier versions.

After migrating Integration Server to a version above 10.5, the
pub.smime.keystore:processEncryptedData service fails to decrypt the S/MIME 
stream encrypted in Integration Server 10.5 or earlier versions, resulting in  
the following error:

com.wm.app.b2b.server.ServiceException: [ISS.0086.9055]Could not retrieve 
content from input

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-83301 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Integration Server does not handle exceptions when the global variable
substitution in a flow service fails.

If there is an issue during the global variable substitution in a flow service, 
Integration Server throws a FlowException. The FlowException is not handled 
by the CATCH block even if the flow service contains a TRY-CATCH block, leading 
to the abrupt termination of the flow service.

This issue is resolved by introducing the following server configuration 
parameter.

watt.server.globalVariables.throwServiceException
Specifies how Integration Server handles exceptions when global variable 
substitution in a flow service fails. When set to true Integration Server 
throws a ServiceException. When set to false Integration Server throws a 
FlowException. If there is a TRY-CATCH block in the flow service, and the 
parameter is set to true, the ServiceException is handled by the CATCH 
block. The default is false.

Integration Server restart is not required for the changes to take effect. 

PIE-83490 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Integration Server incorrectly displays the XML attributes in a generated 
Swagger document.

A Swagger document generated by Integration Server includes fields that start
with '@' instead of treating the fields as attributes in the following
situation: 

- The REST API Descriptor (RAD) is created from a service with a signature that
contains document types defined using XML schemas (that is, 
the XML content type properties are defined).
- The document type includes one or more variables with a name that begins with
the '@' symbol. 
Now, Integration Sever treats the fields that begin with the '@' symbol as
attributes in the generated Swagger document and will include an XML property
definition for such fields. The fields are returned as attributes during runtime
if the media type is in XML format. 

Important:
The variables starting with '@' are treated as an attribute only if the XML 
Content type property is set for the variable. If the variable name starts with 
'@' and the XML content type is not set, then the resulting Swagger document
includes a field name that starts with '@'. 

PIE-83507 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
In rare cases, Integration Server does not store the outbound password for a
consumer web services endpoint alias correctly resulting in an empty password
after the alias is deployed to another Integration Server. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-83521 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Integration Server is indefinitely slow while decoding a document from Universal
Messaging. 

When a webMethods messaging trigger uses protocol buffer encoding to decode a
message containing a byte array, there are instances where Integration Server
encounters the following error: 
IDataProtoBufCoder: decode failure: java.lang.OutOfMemoryError: Java heap space

The issue is resolved. Now, Integration Server uses the same mechanism to encode
and decode the byte array. 

PIE-83560 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Legacy Integration Server Administrator displays an error message for a failed

status failing for: Dry run." at the top even though the most recent metering

PIE-83580 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
In Integration Server, a JDBC pool does not bypass the proxy server when 
connecting to a database.

When configuring the JDBC connection pool, if you have already configured the
default HTTPS proxy server in Integration Server Administrator and if the proxy 
server is enabled, the JDBC pool connects to the database through the proxy
server instead of establishing a direct connection, resulting in a JDBC 
connection failed exception.

This issue is resolved by introducing the following server configuration 
parameter:

watt.server.disableSystemProperty.HPROXY
Specifies whether a JDBC pool should establish a direct connection to a
database. 
If the parameter is set to "true", the JDBC pool establishes a direct connection
to the database, regardless of the default HTTPS proxy server being enabled in
the Integration Server Administrator. The default is "false".

Integration Server restart is required for the changes to take effect.

PIE-83673 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Error responses sent to clients might contain too much information.

When a service ends because of a ServiceException, the error response returned
to a client potentially reveals significant information about the server,
service, and requesting user that could be exploited. The following fields might
be included in a response: $error, $localizedError, $errorType, $stackTrace,
$service, $pipeline, $user, $timestamp, and $contextID. 

Integration Server already includes the watt.server.http.returnException server
configuration parameter which determines whether the $stacktrace is returned to
the client along with the $error (the error message). This fix introduces new
values for watt.server.http.returnException which provide more control over what
information is returned to the calling client. The new values are: 

- brief - Returns all of the fields with the exception of $stackTrace.
- message - Returns $error and $contextID (context ID used for audit logging)
only. This is the most secure option as it returns the least amount of
information. 
- verbose - Returns all of the fields. This is the default.
- webMethods - Returns all of the fields only if the client's HTTP user agent is
set to webMethods or has the same value as the user agent specified in the
watt.net.userAgent parameter. If the user agent in the HTTP request does not
match the watt.net.userAgent value, the response contains $error and $contextID
only. Do not set watt.server.http.returnException to webMethods in a production
environment. A request submitted with the header "User-agent: webMethods" would
return sensitive information that could be misused. 

Note: Previously, the watt.server.http.returnException parameter accepted values
of true and false. These values are still honored. A value of true corresponds
to verbose. A value of false corresponds to brief. 

Note: If a service explicitly sets a response body by invoking
pub.flow:setResponse or pub.flow:setResponse2 and that service end with an
exception, the HTTP response will have a 500 status code but will not contain
the error message, stack trace, or other exception details. The response body
contains only what was set by invoking pub.flow:setResponse or
pub.flow:setResponse2. 

PIE-83691 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
While using pub.xml:documentToXMLString, Integration Server 
encodes single quotes or apostrophes as the decimal equivalent of the ASCII code
instead of the named character entity. 

This issue is resolved. Now, Integration Server uses the named character entity
to escape single quotes or apostrophes. 

PIE-83844 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Invoking pub.date:formatDate as a web service returns the day of the week in the
abbreviated form instead of the complete day name. For example, the service
returns "Sat 23 August 2002" instead of "Saturday 23 August 2002". 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-83909 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Integration Server inconsistently maps the Swagger document variables for
integer and number data type without a format.
 
Consider a Swagger document that contains properties of integer or 
number data type without a format. When creating a REST API Descriptor (RAD)
from such a Swagger document, Integration Server maps the integer or number type
properties as java.math.BigInteger or java.math.BigDecimal respectively. 

This fix provides an option to support the existing implementation of supporting
long and double by introducing the following server configuration parameters: 

watt.server.rest.generateLong

Specifies whether Integration Server maps a property of the integer type 
without a format in a Swagger document to java.lang.Long while creating a RAD. 
When set to true, integer variables without a format are mapped to 
java.lang.Long. The default value is false.

watt.server.rest.generateDouble

Specifies whether Integration Server maps a property of the number type
without a format in a Swagger document to java.lang.Double while creating a RAD. 
When set to true, the number type properties without a format are mapped to 
java.lang.Double. The default value is false.

You do not need to restart Integration Server for changes to the parameters to
take effect.

PIE-84033 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Creating a server alias with SFTP Version 2 client fails.

When using an SFTP Version 2 client to create a server alias, the hostKey is not 
properly encoded in the sftpServerAliases.cnf file. 
As a result, testing the server alias fails with the following exception:

"Failed to test the account with given details.

bounds for length 256"

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-84082 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Integration Server returns the "Access Denied" error when a client invokes a 
REST API through a rad directive that is in a corrupt state. 

When there are changes to a flow service, Integration Server updates the 
associated REST API Descriptor (RAD). However, if the flow service has missing 
constraints, Integration Server fails to handle the null references while 
updating the RAD, which leaves the RAD in a corrupt state. Therefore, when a
client invokes a REST API through the rad directive, Integration Server returns
the "Access Denied" error.

This issue is resolved. Now, Integration Server ignores the missing constraints 
in the flow service, preventing the associated REST resources or services from 
being in a corrupt state, and also logs information about the missing
constraints in the server log.

the service did not include the forwardable headers in the outbound request even
when watt.server.http.forwardHeaders was set to true.

PIE-84266 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)

on the graph instead of the time the Statistics Data Collector indexes the data

PIE-84274 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
If the Integration Server license will expire in less than 30 days, Integration
Server throws a NullPointerException and does not start. 

If the Integration Server licenseKey.xml file will expire in less than 30 days
and watt.server.smtp.userName is set, Integration Server sends an email
notification. When attempting to retrieve the email user's password from the
password store, Integration Server throws a NullPointerException and start up
fails. 

This has been resolved. Integration Server now retrieves the email user's
password from the password store, sends an email notification for the expiring
license, and proceeds with startup. 

PIE-84289 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Integration Server throws DataStoreException while processing a JSON
request.

After upgrading the Jackson libraries, Integration Server fails to process 
JSON strings that exceed 1,000,000 characters in length because of the 
maximum length limit of the upgraded libraries.

This issue is resolved. Now, Integration Server provides the
watt.server.json.decode.maxStringLength parameter to override
the limit on maximum string length. The default value is 2147483647
(the maximum possible value for any integer variable in Java). 
You must restart Integration Server for changes to this parameter
to take effect.

PIE-84291 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Migrating to a higher version of Integration Server fails and the following
appears in the migration.log: Error while initializing JDBC configuration files.
Error message: null. 

This issue is now resolved. 

PIE-84303 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
A service that converts a document (IData) to JSON might fail with an
OutOfMemoryError if the document has a more complex structure and size.

PIE-84347 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Running the Deployer.{bat|sh} script throws
"java.security.cert.CertificateException" 
when Integration Server host and HTTPS port are passed as 
parameters, and the "Require Client Certificates" option is selected in the

PIE-84372 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Integration Server does a reverse DNS lookup during an SSL connection. 

Integration Server does a reverse DNS lookup during an SSL connection with
a client despite having the client's IP address in the "Allow" or "Deny" list for 
port-specific IP access or global IP access.

This issue is resolved by introducing the following server configuration 
parameters:

- watt.server.ipaccess.disableRDNSLookup.global

Specifies whether Integration Server performs a reverse DNS lookup during an SSL
connection with a client if the client's IP address is in the "Allow" or "Deny" 
list for global IP access. When set to "true", Integration Server disables 
the reverse DNS lookup during an SSL connection. The default is false.
Integration Server bypasses the reverse DNS lookup for a client in the 
following situations:

- Global IP Access Setting is "Deny by Default" and "Allow List" has the
    client's IP address.
- Global IP Access Setting is "Allow by Default" and "Deny List" has the
    client's IP address.

Integration Server restart is required for the changes to take effect.

- watt.server.ipaccess.disableRDNSLookup.ports
Specifies a comma-separated list of ports that Integration Server uses to bypass
Reverse DNS lookup of client IP addresses in the "Allow" or "Deny" list while 
establishing an SSL connection with a client. By default, the parameter value is 
blank. Integration Server bypasses the reverse DNS lookup for a client in the 
following situations:

- Port IP Access Setting is "Deny by Default" and "Allow List" has the
    client's IP address.
- Port IP Access Setting is "Allow by Default" and "Deny List" has the
    client's IP address.

Integration Server restart is required for the changes to take effect.

PIE-84380 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
XML transformations that involve external entities pose a security risk.

The issue is resolved. Now, in Integration Server Administrator >
WmXSLT package home page > Samples > CD Catalog Sample, the
blockExternalEntity option is selected by default.

PIE-84414 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Requests without a body might cause a SocketTimeoutException.

HTTP requests using the POST, PUT, PATCH, or DELETE methods can include a body.
For some content types, when these requests are sent to Integration Server
without a body, Integration Server incorrectly waits until the request times out
for the body to be received. 

Now, HTTP requests with no body are processed immediately which prevents the
timeout from occurring. 

PIE-84441 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
The /metrics endpoint returns multiple instances of the metrics
sag_is_service_requests_avg_exec_millis and sag_is_service_requests_total with
different timestamps. 

Now, the /metrics endpoint returns only a single instance of the
sag_is_service_requests_avg_exec_millis and sag_is_service_requests_total
metrics for each IS service. 

Additionally, JVM and server metrics are now based on current data at the time
the /metrics endpoint is called.  In the past, JVM and server metrics were based
on aggregated data that could be several minutes old. 

PIE-84499 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Running a Java service which uses the javax.xml library results in a 
classloader conflict.

The javax.xml library bundled with Integration Server has classes that define 
the APIs for XML processing. However, the JDK used for Integration Server also
provides the same classes. Hence, running a Java service which uses 
the javax.xml library results in a classloader conflict.

This issue is now resolved. 

PIE-84507 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Decoding failure that occurs because the Protocol Buffer descriptor used with
the webMethods messaging trigger cannot be found will now be treated as a
transient error. 

When a webMethods messaging trigger receives a message encoded as a protocol
buffer, the trigger needs the protocol buffer descriptor created for the
publishable document type to decode the message. If the publishable document
type is not loaded at the time of decoding, the decoding fails due to a
MessagingCoderException. The trigger treated the decoding failure as a fatal
error and acknowledged the message to the messaging provider. However, the
decoding failure might be a transient error in some situations, such as when the
package that contains the publishable document type has not yet loaded at the
time the trigger attempts decoding. 

To address this possibility, the trigger now treats a decoding failure that
occurs because the trigger cannot find the protocol buffer descriptor as a
transient error. If a MessagingCoderException occurs, Integration Server can
suspend the trigger and rollback the message when one of the following is true: 

- watt.server.trigger.preprocess.suspendAndRetryOnError=true
- The trigger is configured to suspend and retry later.

Rolling back the message to the provider makes it possible for the trigger to
receive and process the message again later. 

PIE-84550 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Integration Server does not support enumeration constraints when importing a
Swagger document as a provider or consumer. 

Consider a Swagger document that contains enumeration constraints for properties
or parameters. While importing a Swagger document as a provider or consumer,
Integration Server ignores the enumeration constraints, and the document types
and services does not include the defined enumerations. Additionally,
Integration Server ignores the validation for enumerations despite selecting the
"Validate Input" or "Validate Output" checkboxes. 

This issue is resolved. Now, Integration Server supports enumeration if the 
parameter or property type is String. The Content type list displays the 
enumeration constraints, and Integration Server validates the constraints 
at runtime.

PIE-84553 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Improvements for using regular expression to specify the allowed host names for
Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF) checking. 

The existing support for specifying hostnames for SSRF checking was limited in
that it used a special character in java.util.regex as a delimiter, specifically
a comma (,). Integration Server uses java.util.regex for regular expression
pattern matching SSRF host names with the value of the
watt.net.http.ssrf.allowlist server configuration parameter. 

To make it possible to use more powerful regular expressions in
watt.net.http.ssrf.allowlist, Integration Server now includes a server
configuration parameter for setting the delimiter character. Additionally,
Integration Server supports the use of a backslash "\" as an escape
character, allowing the delimiter to be used in the regular expression. 

watt.net.http.ssrf.listDelimiter

Specifies the character to delimit the Java regular expressions in
watt.net.http.ssrf.allowlist. The default is a comma (,). Note that the comma is
s special character in java.util.regex. Specifying a semicolon (;) as the
delimiter allows more powerful expressions to be specified in
watt.net.http.ssrf.alllowlist. If you change the delimiter, make sure to update
the watt.net.http.ssrf.allowlist to use the new delimiter. 

Integration Server needs to be restarted for changes to this parameter to take
effect. 

PIE-84565 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
The references to docTypes are updated incorrectly in REST API Descriptors
(RADs). 

When you generate a RAD from a Swagger document, and move the RAD with
associated assets across folders, some references to document types (docTypes)
are updated incorrectly, leading to issues at runtime. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-84581 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Integration Server throws com.wm.util.coder.InvalidDatatypeException for a REST
request with a datetime value in the request body. 

Consider a REST request that contains a datetime value with a four-digit 
offset, without a colon. For example, "2023-09-01T12:08:40.383+0000". 
Integration Server fails to process such a REST request, resulting in the
exception.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-84629 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Integration Server Administrator console has the vulnerability to content 
injection attacks.

When a client application makes an invalid HTTP request to Integration Server, 
the response to the request contains the invalid URL, which can be misused to 
perform a text injection attack by presenting a customized message to the
application. 

This issue is resolved. Integration Server provides the 
"watt.server.http.404.responseWithURL" server configuration parameter that 
controls the response messages to invalid HTTP requests. 

watt.server.http.404.responseWithURL

Specifies whether Integration Server adds the requested resource name to the 
404 response when a HTTP client sends an invalid URL request. If the parameter
is set to true, Integration Server responds with "Object Not Found (URL name)". 
If the parameter set to false, Integration Server responds with "Object Not
Found". The default value is true. 

You need not restart Integration Server for the changes to the parameter 
to take effect.

PIE-84683 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Enhancements for using master password with a Docker container and a
configuration variables template. 

Integration Server provides the following enhancements for using master
passwords: 

- Changing the master password for an Integration Server running in a Docker
container by supplying the password in the SAG_IS_MASTER_PASSWORD_KEY
environment variable when you start the container. 

- Using the master password as the encryption/decryption key for values in a
configuration variables template (also called an application.properties file).
When the watt.server.configVariables.useMasterKey is set to true and the master
password is 16, 24, or 32 character String, Microservices Runtime (or an
Integration Server with a Microservices license) uses the master password as the
key for encrypting and decrypting values in a configuration variables template.
A more complete description of the parameter follows. 

watt.server.configVariables.useMasterKey
Specifies whether Microservices Runtime uses the master password to encrypt and
decrypt values in a configuration variables template (application.properties
file). Set to true to instruct Microservices Runtime to use the master password
for encrypting and decrypting values in a configuration variables template. Set
to false to use the configuration variables encryption key if one is specified
or fall back to the default encryption key. The default value is false. 

If watt.server.configVariables.useMasterKey is set to true and the master
password is not a 16, 24, or 32 character String, Microservices Runtime uses the
configuration variables encryption key set by the
SAG_IS_CONFIG_VARIABLES_ENC_KEY environment variable or the
configvarsencryptionkey startup switch. If a configuration variables key is not
set, Microservices Runtime falls back to the default encryption key for
encrypting and encrypting configuration variables. 

You must restart Microservices Runtime for changes to this parameter to take
effect. 

PIE-84750 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Setting up an SFTP connection using the application.properties file fails
when the file uses a private key without the passphrase.

The issue is resolved. Now, you can use a private key without the passphrase
in the application.properties file to set up an SFTP connection. This behavior
is similar to that of Integration Server Administrator.

PIE-84761 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Invoking an OpenAPI connector service without the server URL as an
input parameter results in "InvalidInputException: serverURL is a required
field". 

Consider an OpenAPI-based Consumer REST API Descriptor (RAD) 
with an associated connector service that has serverURL as an input field. 
When you run the connector service without providing a value 
for serverURL, Integration Server throws InvalidInputException instead of 
using the list of serverURLs in the RAD.

This issue is now resolved by using the serverURL from the list of
serverURLs in the RAD.

PIE-84838 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Integration Server returns the "Access Denied" error when attempting to connect 
to Integration Server Administrator on the diagnostic port 9999.

After migrating to Integration Server 10.15, attempting to access Integration 
Server Administrator through diagnostic port 9999 results in the "Access Denied" 
error. The error occurs due to the absence of the "wm.server:logout" service in 
the access list for port 9999 in the listeners.cnf file as Integration Server 
uses the service during the startup. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-84954 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Missing null values in OpenAPI-based connector responses.

When you run an OpenAPI-based connector service, if the JSON response from the
REST API contains a field with a null value, the connector output should also
include the field with the null value. However, the null value field is missing
from the connector response. 

This is now resolved.

PIE-84960 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)

PIE-84972 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Change to pub.mime:getEnvelopeStream service to specify whether a MimeMessage or
InputStream will be returned when any of the body parts in the message exceed
the large data threshold. 

Previously, the pub.mime:getEnvelopeStream service always returned a
javax.mail.internet.MimeMessage in the mimeMessage parameter if any of the
message body parts exceed the threshold set by
watt.server.mime.largeDataThreshold server configuration parameter.  Now, the
pub.mime:getEnvelopeStream service includes a new input parameter to indicate if
the Mime message will be returned as a MimeMessage or InputStream if the
threshold is exceeded. 

returnMimeMessage - String. Optional. Specifies whether the Mime message is
returned as a javax.mail.internent.MimeMessage object when any of the body parts
in the message exceed the large date threshold set by the
watt.server.mime.largeDataThreshold. 
Set to:
- yes to return the Mime message in the mimeMessage output parameter as a
MimeMessage when the watt.server.mime.largeDataThreshold is exceeded. This is
the default. 
- no to return the Mime message as an InputStream in the envStream output
parameter when the watt.server.mime.largeDataThreshold is exceeded. 
 
PIE-84999 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
In webMethods.io Integration, while using a filter with a package name to

PIE-85012 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Upgraded jar for Eclipse JGit.

The Eclipse JGit jar included with Integration Server in
<IntegrationServer>/lib/jars has been upgraded to version 6.7.0. The previous
version was 6.3.0. 

This resolves the following known security vulnerability: CVE-2023-4759.

PIE-85053 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Metering simulator now writes service metering log messages to a separate log
file. 

The metering simulator enables the logging of messages for services that would
be metered and therefore generate transaction data when the webMethods Metering
Agent is in use on Integration Server. Previously, the metering simulator wrote
logging data for metered services to the server log. Because the server log can
grow very large and contain data from all the subsystems in Integration Server,
log message for metered services can be hard to find. 

To make it easier to view and analyze service metering data, the metering
simulator now writes to the metering log file.  The metering log is a
comma-separated values file located in:
<IntegrationServer_directory>\instances\<instanceName>\logs 

The frequency with which the metering log rotates is determined by the
watt.server.statsLogRotateInterval, which also controls the statistics log
rotation. Integration Server names the rotated log metering<timestamp>.csv. 

The metering log contains the following fields:
- timestamp: Timestamp at which the metering simulator wrote the log entry to
the metering log. 
- svcName: Name of the top-level service for which the metering simulator is
generating metrics. 
- tenant: The tenantID. If the tenant is null, such as in a self-hosted
runtime, the metering simulator inserts a blank space in the tenant field. 
- user: Name of the user that initiated the transaction.
- duration: Duration of the service, measured in milliseconds.
- trans_count: Number of transactions counted for this single service
invocation. If the duration is less than 3 seconds, the count will be 1. If the
duration exceeds 3 seconds, additional transactions will be counted for each 3
second interval. If your license key determines a different transaction duration
value, the simulator will use that value to determine the number of transactions 

Note: The fields in the metering log are similar to what the metering simulator
previously wrote to the server log with the following differences: 
- user information is now included
- cpu data is not included
- serviceName is now svcName
- transactions is now trans_count

PIE-85105 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Integration Server incorrectly encodes certain characters while updating server 
configuration parameters.

In Integration Server Administrator > Extended settings, each time you update a 
server configuration parameter that contains a single quote, Integration Server 
introduces an additional backslash. 

This issue is now resolved.    

PIE-85221 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
Integration Server now uses PBKDF2, a dedicated password hashing algorithm, to
hash all user passwords. 

The Password-Based Key Derivation Function 2 (PBKDF2) algorithm is a dedicated
password hashing algorithm. After applying this fix, Integration Server uses the
PBKDF2 hashing algorithm for all new user passwords. Integration Server converts
existing passwords, which were hashed using SHA-2, to a PBKDF2 hash when the
password is updated. 

PIE-85240 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
After applying a fix that contains PIE-78321, cached results for service caching
include input fields that have been dropped. 

Now, Integration Server does not include input fields that have been dropped in
cached service results. 

PIE-85400 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
The outbound HTTP interceptor receives a null payload when Integration Server
returns a 401 HTTP response status code

The outbound interceptor logs a "Payload is null" message when Integration 
Server returns a 401 HTTP response status code, even though the outbound call
has a valid response body.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-85433 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
During Integration Server migration from 10.5 to 10.15, the migration
utility throws "java.nio.file.NoSuchFileException" for files at random

PIE-85528 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix8)
When Integration Server receives a REST request for a Swagger-based REST 
resource, Integration Server returns the response based on the Accept header or
Content-Type header. If there is no content handler registered for any of the
media types in the Accept header, Integration Server returns the response as
text/html. 
 
This fix provides the watt.server.rest.useDefaultAccept server configuration 
parameter. When set to false, the parameter gives an option to support the 
existing behavior. When set to true, Integration Server returns the 
response based on the media type values defined in the RAD for the operation.
If one of the media type value in the Accept header is defined in the RAD,
Integration Server returns the response in the same format.
If there is a media type value in the Accept header that is not defined in the 
RAD, Integration Server returns the response in one of the format defined in 
the RAD. If the RAD does not define any media type value, Integration Server 
returns the response as application/json. The default value of the parameter
is false. You do not need to restart Integration Server for changes to this
parameter to take effect.

Depending on the operation system, JDK version, and size of the data stream,
Integration Server incorrectly raises a java.io.EOFException error while
decoding binary String data using the com.wm.util.coder.IDataBinCoder class. 

This issue is now resolved.

DTS-2585

PIE-76505 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix7)
Change in handling of OAuth client secrets in Integration Server.

In Integration Server Administrator, the Security > OAuth > Client registration
> Edit client registration page displays the client_secret generated for a
confidential client in the Secret field. By default, Integration Server masks
the client_secret. However, clicking Reveal Secret displays the client_secret in
clear text. Further, using a browser to inspect an element on the Edit client
registration page allows the client_secret to be viewed. This is a security
vulnerability. 

This fix introduces the following changes to address this security
vulnerability: 

- Upon successful registration of a confidential client, Integration Server
Administrator displays a dialog box containing the generated client_secret. Copy
the client_secret and save it to a secure location. Once the dialog box closes,
you cannot view the client_secret again. 
- The Edit client registration page no longer includes the Secret field and
Reveal Secret button. 
- The Edit client registration page now includes the Generate New Secret button
for a confidential client. Click Generate New Secret to get a new client_secret. 
- The Integration Server Administrator API includes an endpoint for generating a
new client_secret for an existing OAuth client: 
   PUT /admin/oauth/clientsecretupdate

PIE-76876 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix7)
Issue while handling transient error processing.

You can configure Integration Server to retrieve multiple messages from
Universal Messaging for a JMS trigger with each request by using the prefetch
cache. You can enable the prefetch cache by setting the Max prefetch size
property to a value greater than 1 (in the trigger setting). However, the
feature is limited only to concurrent, non-transacted, and non-batched JMS
triggers. The prefetch functionality allows fetching multiple messages
simultaneously and processing them individually. 
Consider that a thread retrieves a batch of messages, and one of them remains
unacknowledged. In such a situation, Integration Server incorrectly indicates
that the remaining messages are acknowledged. These messages are redelivered
causing duplicate processing of the trigger. 

This issue is resolved. Now, Integration Server will skip processing the
remaining messages if any of the message from the prefetch batch is
unacknowledged.

PIE-78723 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix7)
Integration Server log in the JSON format uses additional diskspace due to
anomalies. 

Integration Server log (server.log) in the JSON format has anomalies, such as 
unnecessary white spaces after colons and in some instances after commas. 
The server log takes up additional space due to such anomalies.

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-79162 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix7)
Improvements to Statistics Data Collector for gathering JVM statistics.

The following improvements for gathering and storing JVM statistics are now
available: 

- Increased fault-tolerance and diagnostic logging during statistics collection.
- Compressed storage of metric data in the IS_MONITOR table thus requiring fewer
rows. 
- Server and JVM statistics data are available earlier during the Integration

the Dashboard in Integration Server Administrator. 

This fix also resolves the issue in which some JVM-related Prometheus metrics
where missing when the /metrics endpoint was called.

PIE-81837 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix7)
Collection of JVM statistics appears to stop.
 
The Statistics Data Collector in Integration Server uses data returned by the
JVM statistics collector to populate the JVM metrics tab in the Integration
Server Administrator dashboard. An issue with the JVM might cause the JVM
statistics collector to stop gathering data. 
 
The Statistics Data Collector now periodically checks the state of the JMV
statistics collector and restarts the JVM statistics collector if it has
stopped. 
 
Integration Server now also includes a server configuration parameter that
indicates how soon JVM statistics collection begins after Statistics Data
Collector starts up. 
 
watt.server.statisticsDataCollector.jvmStats.startSecs
Specifies when the Statistics Data Collector begins collecting JVM statistics
once Statistics Data Collector start up completes. The Statistics Data Collector
in Integration Server uses collected JVM statistics to populate the JVM metrics
tab in the Integration Server Administrator dashboard. Specify an integer
greater than or equal to 0.  A value of 0 indicates that JVM statistics
collection begins as soon as the Statistics Data Collector completes its
startup.  The default value is 0. 

For changes to this parameter to take effect, you must either restart
Integration Server or disable and then re-enable statistics data collection for
the Dashboard. 

PIE-81878 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix7)
Migrating from Integration Server 10.5 to 10.15 with custom code that uses AWS

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-82296 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix7)
Integration Server takes a longer time to enter quiesce mode.

Entering quiesce mode, if there are shutdown services while disabling
packages, Integration Server waits for the shutdown services to reach
completion. If there are shutdown services that take longer time 
to complete, Integration Server waits indefinitely.

watt.server.quiesce.force

Specifies whether Integration Server disables a package forcefully. Set the 
parameter value to true to disable the packages forcefully. 
Forcefully disabling a package, terminates the running shutdown services.
Integration Server even terminates the threads for the user-scheduled tasks and
the user-triggered tasks before starting the package disabling. The default
value is false. 

watt.server.quiesce.force.timeout

Specifies the time in milliseconds that Integration Server waits to disable 
each package. If a shutdown service runs longer than the specified time, 
Integration Server terminates the shutdown service. The default value is 
1000 milliseconds.

Important:
Use these parameters cautiously, as forcefully disabling the package 
can result in data loss. Software AG recommends setting a wait time 
of 30 seconds to allow the shutdown services to complete gracefully.

You do not need to restart Integration Server for changes to 
these parameters to take effect.

PIE-82338 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix7)
Addition of classes to the Integration Server whitelist classes file.

Integration Server logs serialization errors for internal webMethods classes and
Java classes because the classes are not part of the Integration Server
whitelist classes file. The server log contains multiple decode errors for
Integration Server such as: 

BinCoder decode error creating Java serialized object.
Excpt:java.lang.ClassNotFoundException: <class_name>, not in White List 

This issue is resolved.

PIE-82999 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix7)
Migrating Microservices Runtime from version 10.11 to 10.15 fails with a

PIE-83008 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix7)
Security log contains password information in clear text for user defined in
Common Directory Services (CDS). 
 
If the security log is enabled and configured to log information about user
creation and/or password changes, creating or updating a user in CDS results in
the user name and password appearing in clear text in the security log in the
Message column. This is a security vulnerability. 

To resolve this issue, Integration Server now includes a server configuration
parameter to hide payload information for user account changes in CDS. By
default, the security log will not include the payload in log entries written
for creating or changing user accounts for CDS users. 

watt.server.securityLog.excludePayload
Specifies whether the Message column in the security log includes the payload
for log entries written for creating or changing user accounts for users in CDS.
Set to true to obscure the payload, which includes the user name and password in
clear text, and display the text "Payload: hidden for security purposes"
instead. Set to false to display the payload in the Message column. The default
value is true, which is more secure. 

Integration Server does not need to be restarted for changes to this parameter
to take effect. 

This parameter does not impact security log entries written for creating or
changing locally defined user accounts or LDAP accounts. Security log entries
for configuration changes to LDAP and local accounts do not include the
password.

subsequently slowing down webMethods.io Integration. 

This issue is resolved by providing an option for webMethods.io

descriptors need checking.

PIE-83387 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix7)
A value placed in cache by a pub.cache* service cannot be retrieved with the key
if a com.wm.data.IData object was used as the key. 
 
If an IData object was used as the key when placing a value in cache using a
pub.cache* service, later attempts to retrieve the value using the same key
might fail. This occurs because IData objects are mutable. 
 
To address this issue, Integration Server now includes the server configuration
parameter watt.server.cache.iDataKey.toString  that specifies whether a
com.wm.data.IData object used as a key in one of the pub.cache* services is
converted to an immutable String before accessing the cache. Set to true to
convert an IData object used as a key to a String. Set to false to keep the key
as an IData object. The default is true. 
 
Integration Server does not need to be restarted for changes to this parameter
to take effect. 
 
Important! If the IData object is modified after it has been used as a key,
Integration Server will not be able to retrieve values stored with the key
regardless of the value of watt.server.cache.iDataKey.toString. 
 
Software AG does not recommend using an IData object as a key with a cache as
IData objects are mutable. Instead, use a java.lang.String object as a key.

PIE-78336 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)
Integration Server uses the graphql-java-9.4.0.jar library, which has the
CVE-2022-37734 vulnerability. For details about the vulnerability, see
https://nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE- 2022-37734 

The issue is resolved. Now, Integration Server uses "graphql-java-17.5.0.jar" 
to address the vulnerability. 

Important: The updated JAR requires significant modifications to the schema 
definitions that were created based on previous versions of the JAR. The 
updated JAR imposes several constraints that affect your schema definitions. 
For example:

Implementing multiple interfaces requires using "&" as a separator instead of a 
comma. 
Two interfaces cannot have a common field name.
Defining a new field by extending a type, interface, or input type is not
permitted. 
Extended scalar types such as Long, Short, Char, BigDecimal, BigInteger are not
implicitly supported. 
Depending on the impact of the updated JAR on your current implementation, you
may need to recreate existing assets or redefine the schema. Given that the 
updated JAR introduces breaking changes, it is strongly recommended that you 
contact Software AG support for assistance with your GraphQL workflows.

PIE-78574 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)
On the Integration Server Administration > Server > Ports > Global IP access 
restrictions > Add hosts to deny/allow page, the specification that a service 
follows is displayed as "pub.security.ports:hostListProviderSpec" instead of 
"pub.security.ports:hostNamesSpec".

Now, the correct specification, "pub.security.ports:hostNamesSpec" is displayed.

PIE-80287 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)
A configuration variables file (application.properties file) is ignored if the

PIE-80434 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)

PIE-80877 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)
Enhancement to customize the HTTP access log format.

You can now configure Integration Server to customize the HTTP access log by 
specifying only the required fields from a predefined list in the order of your
preference. To configure Integration Server to write HTTP log entries according 
to your preferences, the watt.server.httplog server configuration parameter now 
accepts a new value, extended. The new server configuration parameter, 
watt.server.httplog.fields allow you to specify the required fields in the log.

watt.server.httplog.fields
Specifies a comma-separated list of fields that Integration Server logs in 
the HTTP access log. You can specify the fields from a predefined list, and 
in the required order.

For example,
watt.server.httplog=extended
watt.server.httplog.fields=uid(TEST_),'header/X-Forwarded-For',
timestamp(yyyy-MM-dd hh:mm:ss.SSS),method,url,responseCode,serverIp,
clientIp,elapsedTime,responseSize

In the generated log, a space separates the values and the empty field values
are replaced by a hyphen. You can also specify values in double quotes ("") or
single quotes (''). If the provided field is not from the predefined list, then
Integration Server ignores the field.

The predefined list of fields:

uid (Unique ID for a log entry based on timestamp. You can also
prepend a prefix to the ID. For example, uid(SAG_)) 
host
protocol
username
timestamp (You can also specify the format. For example, timestamp (yyyy-mm-dd))
request
responseCode
responseSize
referer
userAgent
elapsedTime
serverIp
clientIp
method
url
header/<HeaderName> (Logs the HTTP header <HeaderName> that is available in 
the request.)

PIE-81307 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)
Integration Server returns an unexpected Content-Type in the response to
a REST request.

Integration Server responds with the Content-Type as text/html to a REST
request that has the Accept header as /. However, the Content-Type in the
response must be the first value in the Produces section of the REST API
Descriptor.

This issue is now resolved. 

PIE-81443
While monitoring tenant connections, Integration Server retains the session 
context even if there are errors after creating a session context, which 
might cause a session leakage.

This issue is resolved. Now, Integration Server removes the session context 
for errors as well.

PIE-81644 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)
Terracotta Server Array removes an Integration Server from the cluster due to
excessive session expirations. 

When a session expires, Integration Server updates the SessionStore cache which
is unnecessary because Ehcache manages expiration of cache elements.
Additionally, it creates work for the SessionStore cache. In a cluster, the
Integration Server update to the SessionStore cache generates unnecessary cache
event notifications that have to be processed by Integration Server. When this
load on the SessionStore cache is very high, Integration Server can become
temporarily unresponsive, causing the Terracotta Server Array to remove the
Integration Server instance from the cluster. 

This fix removes the unnecessary update by to the SessionStore cache made by
Integration Server when a session expires. In turn, this eliminates the cache
event notifications for session expiration, which improves server performance.
As a result, Integration Server will no longer be removed from a cluster due to
excessive session expiration processing. 

PIE-81707 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)
Blocked services lead to performance degradation in Integration Server
connected to a slow SFTP server.

When multiple services in Integration Server connect to SFTP servers, the service 
that connects to a slow SFTP server blocks the rest. 

This issue is now resolved.

PIE-81750 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)
If Integration Server receives a request with an invalid URL and a Cookie header
that identifies a session, subsequent requests that use the session are rejected
with a 401 status code. 

When a request with an invalid URL is sent to Integration Server, and the
request includes a Cookie header that identifies a session, the session becomes
unusable. Integration Server rejects all subsequent requests that use the
session with a 401 status code. 

This issue has been resolved. When a request with an invalid URL is sent to
Integration Server, it is rejected but the session is retained and can be used
in subsequent requests.

PIE-82224 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)
Resolved issues for webMethods messaging.
 
This fix addresses the following issues in webMethods messaging:

- The request-reply channel for a stateless Integration Server has a new ID
every time Integration Server starts. Over time, this results in a build-up of
request-reply channels on Universal Messaging. 
- Integration Server does not honor the value of the Enable Request-Reply
Channel and Listener check box. 
- Refreshing triggers is not thread safe and might cause messages to be stuck
until the Universal Messaging connection alias restarts. 

The following paragraphs provide more information about these changes.

Persisting of Request-Reply Channel ID for a Stateless Integration Server
In webMethods messaging, Integration Server uses a dedicated request-reply
channel and listener. The channel name includes a unique ID generated the first
time that Integration Server starts. However, if Integration Server is stateless
(for example, when running in a stateless container), the generated ID is not
saved to disk and does not persist across server restarts. This results in the
creation of new request-reply channel on Universal Messaging every time
Integration Server restarts. Over time, the unused channels build up on
Universal Messaging. (A stateful Integration Server persists the unique ID to
disk and uses the same request-replay channel name across restarts.) 

To prevent the build up of unused request-reply channels, Integration Server
provides a configuration option to automatically delete the request-reply
channel when the connection to Universal Messaging is lost. Set
watt.server.messaging.requestReply.useTempChannel to true to delete the
dedicated request-reply channel and listener shortly after the connection to
Universal Messaging is closed (this occurs when the alias is stopped). If the
connection to Universal Messaging is lost and then restored quickly (that is,
before the channel is deleted), Integration Server uses the same request-reply
channel. Setting watt.server.messaging.requestReply.useTempChannel to true
effectively makes the request-reply channel a temporary channel. Set
watt.server.messaging.requestReply.useTempChannel to false to keep the
request-reply channel on Universal Messaging across restarts of the Integration
Server. 
Integration Server does not need to be restarted for changes to this parameter
to take effect. 
 
Enable Request-Reply Channel and Listener check box
In Integration Server Administrator, the use of a dedicated request-reply
channel and listener can be configured on a per connection alias basis via the
Enable Request-Reply Channel and Listener check box. However, Integration Server
ignored the check box configuration and a dedicated channel and listener was
always used. 
Now, Integration Server honors the value of the Enable Request-Reply Channel and
Listener check box. If the check box is cleared, Integration Server does not use
a dedicated request-reply channel to retrieve replies to requests sent using the
connection alias. 
 
Thread Safety when Refreshing webMethods Messaging Triggers
When a channel is manually deleted or edited on Universal Messaging during
runtime and when an Integration Server is connected to the channel, Integration
Server refreshes the trigger automatically. However, the act of refreshing the
trigger is not thread-safe and could result in the creation of two listeners for
the same trigger on the channel. As a result, messages could get stuck in the
trigger queue and remain unprocessed until the messaging connection alias used
by the trigger was refreshed. This thread-safety issue could also occur when
Designer is used to edit a trigger. 

Now, refreshing a trigger in the above scenarios are thread-safe which prevents
messages from becoming stuck in the trigger queue.

PIE-82325 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)

following properties.

SFTP User Alias properties

sftpuser.aliasName.authenticationType : password or public key.
sftpuser.aliasName.privateKeyFileLocation : location of the private key if 
authenticationType is public key.
sftpuser.aliasName.strictHostKeyChecking : yes or no.
sftpuser.aliasName.passPhrase : passphrase generated while creating the private 
key.

SFTP Server Alias properties

sftpserver.aliasName.version : v1 or v2
sftpserver.aliasName.preferredKeyExchangeAlgorithm: key exchange algorithms 
separated by a comma.
sftpserver.aliasName.hostKey : location of the public key of the SFTP server.
sftpserver.aliasName.preferredMACS2C : preferred Mac S2C algorithms separated by
a comma. 
sftpserver.aliasName.preferredMACC2S : preferred Mac C2S algorithms separated by
a comma. 
sftpserver.aliasName.preferredCiphersS2C : preferred S2C ciphers separated by a
comma. 
sftpserver.aliasName.preferredCiphersC2S : preferred C2S  ciphers separated by a
comma. 
sftpserver.aliasName.minDHKeySize=Integer value representing the key size in
bytes. 
For example, 1024
sftpserver.aliasName.maxDHKeySize=Integer value representing the key size in
bytes. 
For example, 8192

PIE-82441 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)

which leads to issues specifically with Ubuntu POSIX.

PIE-82709 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)
As part of this fix, Integration Server supports creating global variables at 
the server level or package level. All services in Integration Server have
access to a server-level global variable, while a package-level global variable
is only accessible by services within the package that has the global variable 
defined.

You can create global variables using Integration Server Administrator. In 
Settings > Global variables, add a package to which you can save the global 
variable definition. If you specify a package, Integration Server creates a 
package-level global variable; else Integration Server creates a server-level 
global variable. 

The location where Integration Server saves a global variable depends on 
whether it is a server-level or package-level global variable.

For server-level global variables, the variable definition is saved in:
Integration Server_directory\instances\instance_name\config\globalVariables.cnf

For package-level global variables, the variable definition is saved in the 
package in:
Integration Server_directory\instances\instance_name\packages\package_name\config\ 
globalVariables.cnf
When Integration Server encounters global variable substitution during service 
execution, Integration Server first looks for the global variable defined at the 
package level. If not found, Integration Server looks for the global variable 
at the server level. 

However, you can override this default behavior by specifying whether the 
service must use a server-level or a package-level global variable. To use 
a server-level global variable, prefix the variable name like this: 
%server:variablename%. To use a package-level global variable, prefix the 
variable name like this: %package:variablename%.

The server-level or package-level global variables can be created or edited 
using the configuration variables template. The assets and property names that 
correspond to the key names in the template are as follows:

Asset: Global Variable (Package-Level)
Property: Value, Key Name: globalvariable.packageName.globalVariableName.value
Property: Is Password?, Key Name:
globalvariable.packageName.globalVariableName.isSecure 
Set to true to indicate the global variable is secure or a password. 
Asset: Global Variable (Server-Level)    
Property: Value, Key Name: globalvariable.globalVariableName.value
Property: Is Password?, Key Name: globalvariable.globalVariableName.isSecure
           Set to true to indicate the global variable is secure or a password.

PIE-82764 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)
The "wm.server.dispatcher:deleteExpiredUUID" service causes

PIE-82855 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)
When decoding a large XML document with a deep tag structure, Integration Server
may become unresponsive. 
 
When Integration Server decodes an XML document, the XMLCoder inserts spaces for
indenting for each level of XML tag and newlines. When decoding a large XML
document with a deeply nested tag structure, the XMLCoder may be attempting to
insert thousands of spaces and newlines to show hierarchy. While this "pretty"
processing makes the XML more human readable when viewed in a text editor, it
may cause Integration Server to become unresponsive. 
 
To mitigate this issue, Integration Server now includes the ability to disable
pretty processing by the XMLCoder. When the XMLCoder perform pretty processing,
it inserts spaces and new lines, making the XML more readable when viewed in a
text editor. If pretty processing is not performed, the XMLCoder does not insert
spaces or newlines. When viewed in a text editor, the resulting XML appears as a
long string and is not very human readable. 

Integration Server now includes a special HTTP header to disable the pretty
function when the XMLCoder decodes an XML document received in a request.  When
an incoming request includes the header $$$webm-xmlcoder-pretty:false, the
XMLCoder does not perform pretty processing for nested tags. That is, the
XMLCoder does not insert spaces for XML tag level indentation or newlines. This
may prevent Integration Server from becoming unresponsive when XMLCoder
processes a large XML document with deeply nested tags. If the incoming request
does not include the header $$$webm-xmlcoder-pretty or includes
$$$webm-xmlcoder-pretty:true, the XMLCoder performs the pretty processing. 
 
In addition, the com.wm.util.coder.XMLCoder class now includes the following
methods that can be used when decoding XML documents from Java services. 

setPretty (Boolean enabled)
Sets a Boolean flag that specifies whether XMLCoder insert a space for each
nested tag level when processing an XML document. 
Parameters:
pretty - A Boolean specifying whether the XMLCoder performs pretty processing.
Set to enabled for the XMLCoder to perform pretty processing by inserting a
space for each nested tag level. Set to disabled to skip pretty processing. 
 
isPretty( )
Returns a Boolean indicating if the XMLCoder performs pretty processing by
inserting a space for each nested tag level when processing an XML document. 
Returns pretty=enabled if pretty processing is enabled. Else returns
pretty=disabled.

PIE-82903 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)
Changes to webMethods Metering for hybrid integration.

The webMethods Metering Agent considers execution of top-level user-defined
services to be metered transactions. For metering purposes, a hybrid integration
in which webMethods Cloud invokes a service residing on an on-premise
Integration Server does not count as a metered transaction despite it being a
top-level service invocation. 

PIE-82939 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix6)
Incorrect inactiveCount flag in the log messages of webMethods messaging
triggers. 

In the log messages of webMethods messaging triggers, there is an 
"inactiveCount" flag that indicates the number of times the trigger's poll for 
a message is inactive. However, Integration Server does not reset the 
flag when the trigger successfully processes a new message. As a result, the
inactiveCount keeps incrementing, suggesting a high count for the flag. 

This issue is resolved. Now, Integration Server resets the flag to zero when 
webMethods messaging trigger receives a message for processing.

PIE-80444 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix5)
A service that uses a multi-release JAR file throws 
java.lang.reflect.InvocationTargetException.

In a multi-release JAR file, if the base class and a version-
specific class in the META-INT/versions/<JDK major version>/directory have 
different names, and the class files are also not available in the top-level 
directory, the service throws the exception.

Applying this fix removes the restriction on using the same name for base-
version and specific-version classes allowing the JRE (Java Runtime Environment) 
to use the correct class along with the version of the class corresponding to 
the JRE version used.

PIE-81099 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix5)
An OpenAPI REST request from Integration Server to the provider with an
undefined Accept header results in UnsupportedMediatypeException.

An OpenAPI document can have multiple HTTP status codes in an operation
response. Each HTTP status code can have multiple media types defined.
Consider a request that has an Accept header value, which is not defined for
the HTTP status code. Such a request results in UnsupportedMediatypeException.

This issue is now resolved. Now, Integration Server responds with the first
media type defined for the HTTP status code. This behavior is not applicable 
for HTTP status code in 2xx.

PIE-82061 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix5)
After applying a fix that includes PIE-77728,  executing the pub.io:reset 
service results in the "java.io.IOException: Stream closed" error.

The resolution for PIE-77728 changed the pub.io:streamToString service to close 
the input stream. Consequently, if the pub.io:reset service uses the same
inputStream used by pub.io:streamToString, the pub.io:reset service fails 
because the stream is already closed. The pub.io:reset service ends with the
error: java.io.IOException: Stream closed.

To resolve this issue, the pub.io:streamToString service no longer closes the 
inputStream. Invoke pub.io:close to close the input stream.

PIE-76455 (IS_10.15_Core_Fix4)
